The Second Proof: Miracles of the Prophet
Al-Sawi enumerates miracles of the Prophet as the second proof of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the miracles of the Prophet and his character together constitute the second proof of his prophethood, and why the transmission of these miracles is considered reliable.

Core Idea
Miracles and character together prove prophethood beyond doubt.

In this lesson, we explore the second proof of prophethood presented by al-Sawi: the miracles (khawariq al-'adat) of the Prophet Muhammad. He argues that these miracles are widely transmitted and that the Prophet's flawless character further confirms his truthfulness. We'll examine the evidence and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Note the two main components: miracles and character.
The passage is dense with examples.
2
Understand the transmission argument
The author says the miracles have reached tawatur in their common core, even if details are ahad. Why is this important for establishing proof?
Tawatur means multiple chains leading to certainty.
3
Reflect on the character evidence
The author describes the Prophet's beautiful character and specific qualities. How does this complement the miraculous evidence?
Character alone can convince observers of truthfulness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانيهما : أنّه نُقل عنه عليه الصَّلاة والسَّلام من خوارق العادات ما بلغ القدر المشترك من حد التواتر وإن كان تفاصيلها آحاداً ؛ كتسبيح الحصى في كفّه، وتكليم الجمادات والحيوانات، ونبع الماء من الأصابع، وظهور البركة في الأطعمة والأشربة، وغير ذلك مما لا يحصى كثرة . مع ما كان عليه من حُسْن الخُلُق، الذي لا يراه أحد إلا ويقطع أنه ليس بكذاب، وإن كان يقع من الضَّالين العناد. ومن كمال خلقه تمام الحلم والعلم مع كونه ولد في قوم لا يعرفون شيئاً، من غير أن يتعاطى أسباب العلم، ووفور البركة، مع قلة الأكل جداً، فيقدم حيث تحجم الأبطال، ويقف حيث يفر الأبطال عند شدّة.
The second: It has been transmitted from him (peace and blessings be upon him) of extraordinary things that reached the common denominator of the limit of tawatur (widespread transmission), even if their details are isolated reports; such as the glorification of pebbles in his hand, the speech of inanimate objects and animals, the gushing of water from his fingers, the appearance of blessing in food and drink, and other things uncountable. Along with his beautiful character, which no one sees except that he is certain that he is not a liar, even if obstinacy occurs from the misguided. And from the perfection of his character is complete forbearance and knowledge despite being born among a people who knew nothing, without him pursuing the means of knowledge, and abundance of blessing, with very little eating, he would advance where heroes hesitate, and stand where heroes flee during intensity.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof of prophethood: the miracles (khawariq al-'adat) of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author argues that these miracles have reached the level of tawatur (massively transmitted) in their overall common core, even though the specific details of each miracle may come through isolated reports (ahad). He then lists examples: the glorification of pebbles in the Prophet's hand, the speech of inanimate objects and animals, water flowing from his fingers, and blessings appearing in food and drink. These are just a sample of countless miracles. The author then adds that the Prophet's perfect character is further evidence: anyone who sees him is certain he is not a liar, despite the obstinacy of some. He was born among an ignorant people without formal education, yet he possessed complete forbearance and knowledge, and he exhibited abundant blessings despite eating very little. In battle, he would advance where heroes hesitated and stand firm where they fled. This character, combined with the miracles, conclusively proves his prophethood.

Correction: The author clarifies that the common core of miracles reaching tawatur is sufficient; details may be ahad.

The Miracle of the Speaking Lizard
Narrates the miracle of a lizard speaking to testify to the Prophet's authenticity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the miracle of the speaking lizard serves as a proof of prophethood and the rational basis for accepting such narrated miracles.

Core Idea
A lizard's speech confirmed the Prophet's mission, and a Bedouin believed.

This lesson presents a remarkable narrated miracle where a lizard speaks to testify to the truth of Prophet Muhammad (SAW). The story demonstrates that miracles can occur through non-human agents as clear signs from Allah. Let's examine the narrative and its significance as evidence for prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the story carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the sequence of events.
Notice the dialogue between the Prophet and the lizard.
2
Identify the miracle
Observe that the lizard speaks with a clear tongue and answers theological questions about worship and the Prophet's identity.
The lizard's speech is a direct violation of natural laws.
3
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how this miracle led to the Bedouin's conversion and how it is used as evidence for the truth of Islam.
Think about why a non-human creature's testimony is so powerful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقال الأعرابي : من هذا؟ قالوا : نبي الله ، فقال : واللات والعزى، لا آمنت به إلا أن يؤمن هذا الضب، وطرحه بين يديه صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: «يا ضب»، فأجابه بلسان مبين يسمعه القوم جميعاً : لبيك وسعديك يا زين من وافى يوم القيامة، قال: «من تعبد؟» قال : الذي في السماء عرشه، وفي الأرض سلطانه، وفي البحر سبيله، وفي الجنة رحمته، وفي النار عقابه قال: «فمن أنا ؟»، قال رسول رب العالمين، وخاتم النبيين، وقد أفلح من صدقك، وخاب من كذبك، فأسلم الأعرابي. أخرجه الطبراني فى «الأوسط» (٥٩٩٦) ، والبيهقي في الدلائل)) ((٣٧/٦) عن عمر بن الخطاب
The Bedouin said: 'Who is this?' They said: 'The Prophet of Allah.' He said: 'By al-Lat and al-Uzza, I will not believe in him unless this lizard believes.' He threw it before him, peace be upon him, and he said: 'O lizard!' So it answered with a clear tongue that all the people heard: 'At your service and at your pleasure, O ornament of those who come on the Day of Resurrection.' He said: 'Whom do you worship?' It said: 'He whose throne is in the heaven, Whose dominion is on earth, Whose path is in the sea, Whose mercy is in Paradise, Whose punishment is in Hell.' He said: 'Who am I?' It said: 'The Messenger of the Lord of the worlds, and the Seal of the Prophets; successful is he who believes you, and lost is he who disbelieves you.' So the Bedouin became Muslim. Al-Tabarani narrated it in al-Awsat (5996), and al-Bayhaqi in al-Dala'il (6/37) from Umar ibn al-Khattab.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a narrative proof of prophethood through a specific miracle: a lizard speaking to testify to Muhammad (SAW). It begins with a Bedouin who, seeing the Prophet, declares he will only believe if a certain lizard converts. The Prophet calls the lizard, and it speaks eloquently, answering his questions about worship and identifying him as the Messenger of God and the Seal of the Prophets. The lizard's speech causes the Bedouin to embrace Islam. The story is attributed to al-Tabarani and al-Bayhaqi, showing it is drawn from reliable hadith sources. This miracle directly demonstrates divine support for the Prophet, as a non-human creature confirms his message.

Correction: The story is cited as an authentic miracle from reliable hadith sources (al-Tabarani, al-Bayhaqi) and is used as evidence for prophethood.

Checkpoint

B) That a specific lizard believe in him.

D) That all lizards convert.

Key Takeaway
The lizard's speech is an authentic miracle that demonstrates divine confirmation of Muhammad's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Despite witnessing the miracle, the Bedouin could have hardened his heart, but he immediately embraced Islam. Is there a truth you have recognized but not yet acted upon? What fear or attachment is holding you back from taking that step of faith today?

Prophethood of Other Prophets: Known through Revelation
Explains that prophethood of other prophets is known from revelation and they share the same obligations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophethood of other prophets is known through revelation and that they share the same essential attributes as Prophet Muhammad.

Core Idea
Prophethood of all prophets is known from revelation, not reason.

This passage addresses how we know about the prophethood of prophets other than Muhammad. It clarifies that this knowledge comes from the Quran and Sunnah, and emphasizes that all prophets share the same fundamental qualities. The passage also notes that some prophets are specifically named in the Quran, totaling twenty-five.

Guided Path

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا نُبوَّة غيره كآدم فمن بعده : فقد عُلم بالكتاب والسُّنَّة، وأثنى عليهم الله تعالى في كتابه بقوله : رُسُلًا مُبَشِّرِينَ وَمُنذِرِينَ (١) ، وغير ذلك، فيجب لهم ما يجب له عليه الصَّلاة والسَّلام، والبعض قد عيَّنه الكتاب. قوله : (والبعض قد عيَّنه الكتاب) أي وهو خمسة وعشرون؛ منهم

This clarifies the Islamic doctrine that all prophets share the same essential qualities and are recognized through divine revelation.

Tawatur of the Prophet's Miracles
The author states that the Prophet's qualities are transmitted via tawatur, giving necessary knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet's miraculous qualities are transmitted via tawatur, yielding necessary knowledge that rational people cannot deny.

Core Idea
The Prophet's miracles are known by necessary knowledge through tawatur.

This passage from the text explains how the miraculous qualities of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) have been transmitted to us. The author argues that the transmission is so widespread and consistent that it produces certain knowledge. Let's explore the reasoning and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic source passage and its literal translation to get a feel for the author's argument.
Notice the vivid language describing the Prophet's courage.
2
Identify the claim
The passage begins by describing the Prophet's steadfastness and the testimony of both friend and foe. Identify how this supports the main argument.
3
Understand tawatur
The author states that all this was transmitted via tawatur, giving necessary knowledge. Consider what tawatur means and why it yields certainty.
Tawatur is a technical term in Islamic epistemology meaning concurrent testimony that precludes collusion.
4
Reflect on the consequence
The passage ends with a warning about those who deny this known truth. Think about why such denial is considered deserving of punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معجزاته عليه الصَّلاة والسلام
الهول صناديدُ الرّجال، ويثبت على حاله من الدعوى لدى شدائد الأهوال، حتّى لم يجد أعداؤه إليه مطعناً في حال من الأحوال، بل شهد له العدوُّ والحبيب بوُفُور الكمال والإفضال.
كلُّ ذلك نُقل إلينا بالتواتر، فعلمنا ذلك علماً ضرورياً ، فلا يُعاند في ذلك إلا مَن استحق من الله تعالى شديد التكال .
His miracles, peace and blessings be upon him: The lions of men, and he remains steadfast in his claim in the face of severe terrors, until his enemies found no criticism against him in any condition. Rather, both enemy and friend testified to his abundant perfection and bounty. All of that was transmitted to us via tawatur, so we know it by necessary knowledge. No one opposes that except one who deserves from Allah Almighty severe punishment.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage discusses the miraculous qualities of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and their transmission. It begins by describing his extraordinary courage and steadfastness in his claim of prophethood, such that even his enemies could find no fault. Both friend and foe acknowledged his perfection. Then it states that all these qualities have been transmitted to us through tawatur—concurrent testimony that yields certainty. This knowledge is necessary (ḍarūrī), meaning rational people cannot rationally deny it. The only people who reject it are those who deserve severe punishment from Allah.

Key Terms
تواتر (tawatur)
علم ضروري (necessary knowledge)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that knowledge from tawatur is merely probable.
Correction: The author stresses it is necessary knowledge (ḍarūrī) that yields certainty.

Checkpoint

A) Through rational deduction
B) Through tawatur (concurrent transmission) giving necessary knowledge
C) Through personal observation
D) Through mystical unveiling

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's miraculous qualities are known with certainty through tawatur, and denying them is a grave error.

?

Prophethood of Others through Revelation
The author explains the source of knowledge for prophethood of other prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the prophethood of all prophets besides Muhammad (peace be upon him) is known through the Quran and Sunnah, not necessarily through witnessed miracles, and that we must believe in all of them, though some are specifically named in the Quran while others are not.

Core Idea
Revelation, not miracles, is the primary source for knowing earlier prophets.

In this passage, the author turns from the prophethood of Muhammad to that of other prophets. How do we know that figures like Adam were truly prophets? The answer is through the Quran and Sunnah. The author clarifies that the same obligations of belief apply to all prophets, and distinguishes between those explicitly named in the Quran and those left unspecified.

Guided Path

Read the Arabic source

The author states that what is obligatory for Muhammad is obligatory for them (belief, respect). Then he notes that some are specified in the Book (like the 25 prophets named in the Quran), while others are not specified, so we must believe in them generally.
This means we affirm the prophethood of all prophets without needing to know their names.

The Finality of Prophethood with Muhammad
The author asserts that Muhammad is the last prophet, proven by Quran and Sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the finality of prophethood with Muhammad is established by the Quran and Sunnah, and that no new prophethood can begin after him.

Core Idea
Muhammad is the seal of the prophets—no prophet after him.

This lesson focuses on a core belief in Islam: that Prophet Muhammad is the last prophet. The author cites the Quran and Sunnah as the sources for this doctrine, and explains its implication: no new prophethood can be initiated after him. This teaching is fundamental to the Islamic creed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style of the author.
2
Identify the two sources mentioned
The passage says 'by the Book and the Sunnah' – these are the Quran and the Prophet's traditions. These are the primary sources of Islamic knowledge.
3
Understand the implication
The conclusion is that no prophethood begins after Muhammad. Think about why this is important for the Islamic creed.
This refutes any claim to prophethood after him.
4
Reflect on the significance
This belief distinguishes Islam from other faiths that accept later prophets. Consider how it impacts the concept of finality.
5
Check your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you've grasped the main point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ثبت بالكتاب والسُّنَّة أنّه آخر النبيِّين ، فلا تُبتدأ نُبوَّةٌ بعده عليه الصلاة والسلام
And it has been established by the Book and the Sunnah that he is the last of the prophets, so no prophethood is initiated after him, peace and blessings be upon him.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This is a straightforward doctrinal statement: it is established by the Quran and Sunnah that Muhammad is the final prophet. The conclusion is that no new prophethood can begin after him. This refutes any claim of prophethood after Muhammad, and it is a core Sunni belief.

Key Terms
آخر النبيين (last of the prophets)
خاتم النبيين (seal of the prophets)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

Correction: This passage explicitly states that no prophethood is initiated after him. The Quran and Sunnah confirm finality.

Key Takeaway

The King's Council Analogy for Prophethood
An analogy to explain how miracles prove prophethood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the analogy of a king's council illustrates the necessary knowledge that miracles provide for confirming a prophet's truthfulness.

Core Idea
A miracle is like a king breaking his own custom to prove his messenger is truthful.

In this passage, the author uses a vivid analogy to make the logical force of miracles tangible. Imagine a man in a king's court claiming to be the king's messenger. The only proof that convinces everyone is the king himself breaking his usual behavior. This analogy shows why miracles—acts that break natural customs—are immediate and necessary proofs of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the analogy carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the scenario: a claimant, a king, an assembly, and a request for proof.
The Arabic after 'ويقعد' is garbled, but the core analogy is complete.
2
Identify the roles and their counterparts
Map the analogy: the king corresponds to God, the claimant to a prophet, and the assembly to the people. The 'habit' is the natural order (ʿāda).
3
Understand 'changing habit' as a miracle
The king breaking his habit by standing up is an extraordinary act that only the king can do. Similarly, a miracle is a custom-breaking act that only God can perform.
This is the essence of the proof.
4
Reflect on necessary knowledge
The passage says this knowledge is 'ḍarūrī' (necessary) — the connection between the miracle and truthfulness is immediately obvious, not requiring reasoning.
Think about why a king would not break his habit for a liar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ضرب الأشياخ لصدق مدَّعي الرّسالة بدليل المعجزة مثالاً يتّضح به دلالتها على صدقه ويُعلم ذلك بالضرورة، فقالوا : مثال ذلك ما إذا قام رجل في مجلس مَلِك بحضور جماعة وادّعى أنَّه رسول هذا المَلِك إليهم، فطلبوا منه الحُجَّة على ذلك، فقال : دليلي على صدق قولي أن يُغيّر المَلِك عادته ؛ بأن يقوم عن سريره، ويقعد
And the masters (ashyākh) gave an example for the truthfulness of the claimant to prophethood through the evidence of a miracle, by which its indication of his truthfulness becomes clear, and that is known by necessity. They said: The example of that is when a man stands up in a king's assembly in the presence of a group and claims that he is a messenger of this king to them. They ask him for proof of that. He says: My proof for the truth of my statement is that the king changes his habit; by getting up from his throne and sitting down.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage presents an illustrative analogy used by the scholars (ashyākh) to explain how a miracle proves the truthfulness of a claimant to prophethood. The analogy: a man in a king's court claims to be the king's messenger. To prove it, he asks the king to break his usual custom, e.g., getting up from his throne and sitting down in an unusual manner. If the king does that, it is a sign that the man is indeed his messenger, because the king would not break his habit for a liar. Similarly, a prophet performs a miracle which breaks the natural custom (ʿāda), and only God can do that, so it confirms the prophet's truthfulness. The knowledge from this is necessary (ḍarūrī), meaning it is immediately obvious.

Key Terms
معجزة (miracle)
عادة (custom/habit)
علم ضروري (necessary knowledge)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that miracles are merely extraordinary events that can be explained naturally.
Correction: The analogy shows that miracles are custom-breaking signs from God, directly indicating a prophet's truthfulness, not just natural anomalies.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

The author notes unspecified prophets and affirms finality of prophethood.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Muhammad is the last prophet; no new prophethood after him.

The author concludes his discussion on the prophets by noting that while twenty-five are named, some are left unspecified. He then reaffirms the core Islamic belief that Muhammad is the seal of the prophets, established by both the Qur'an and Sunna.

Example of a Miracle as Proof of Prophethood
Scholars illustrate how a miracle proves a claimant's truthfulness with a king analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a miracle serves as a definitive proof of a prophet's truthfulness through the scholars' illustrative example.

Core Idea
A miracle is like a king breaking his habit - it produces certain knowledge.

The scholars of theology often use analogies to clarify difficult concepts. In this passage, they present a powerful example that shows how an extraordinary act can yield certainty about a claimant's truthfulness. This lesson will walk you through that analogy and explain its logical force.

Guided Path
1
Read the analogy
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the story. Note the setting: a king's assembly.
Focus on the claimant's demand and the king's action.
2
Identify the parallel
Notice how the claimant's demand (the king changes his habit) parallels a prophet's miracle (breaking the natural order).
The miracle is the proof; the change in habit is the sign.
3
Understand the certainty
The passage says the group obtains necessary knowledge (al-ʿilm al-ḍarūrī). Ask yourself: why is this certain, not just probable?
The direct observation of the impossible act forces conviction.
4
Extend the lesson
Consider that even those who hear the report via tawātur get the same certainty. This shows how miracles remain proof for later generations.
Tawātur ensures the transmission is reliable and unbroken.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ضرب الأشياخ لصدق مدَّعي الرّسالة بدليل المعجزة مثالاً يتّضح به دلالتها على صدقه ويُعلم ذلك بالضرورة، فقالوا : مثال ذلك ما إذا قام رجل في مجلس مَلِك بحضور جماعة وادّعى أنَّه رسول هذا المَلِك إليهم، فطلبوا منه الحُجَّة على ذلك، فقال : دليلي على صدق قولي أن يُغيّر المَلِك عادته ؛ بأن يقوم عن سريره، ويقعد ثلاث مرات، والمَلِك ذلك، ففعل المَلِك ذلك، فلا شكّ أنّه يحصل للجماعة العلمُ الضَّروريُّ أنَّه صادق في دعواه، ومُنزَّل منزلة قوله : (صدق هذا الرَّجل فيما ادعاه) ولا فرق في حصول العلم بذلك لمن شاهده أو لم يشاهده، ولكن نُقل إليه خبر هذا الفعل بالتواتر .
And the scholars have given an example of the proof of a claimant to prophethood through a miracle, by which its indication of his truthfulness becomes clear and is known necessarily. They said: An example of that is when a man stands in the assembly of a king in the presence of a group and claims that he is the messenger of this king to them. They ask him for proof of that, so he says: My proof of the truth of my statement is that the king should change his habit by rising from his throne and sitting three times, and the king [does] that. So the king does that. There is no doubt that necessary knowledge is obtained for the group that he is truthful in his claim, and it is given the rank of [the king] saying: 'This man is truthful in what he claimed.' And there is no difference in the obtaining of knowledge of that between one who witnessed it or did not witness it, but rather the report of this action was transmitted to him via tawatur.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage presents an illustrative example that clarifies how a miracle functions as proof of a prophet's truthfulness. The scholars (al-ashyākh) use a simile: a man claims to be a king's messenger to a group. The group demands proof. The claimant says his proof is that the king should break his usual custom by standing up and sitting down three times. When the king actually does so, the group necessarily knows that the claimant is truthful—this is not just probable but certain knowledge (al-ʿilm al-ḍarūrī). The analogy: the miracle is an act that breaks the normal course of nature, performed by God in support of a prophet's claim. Just as the group's immediate knowledge is certain, so too is the knowledge that a miracle confirms a prophet. The passage further notes that this certain knowledge is obtained equally by eyewitnesses and by those who receive the report through mutawātir transmission (tawātur), i.e., a continuous, unbroken chain of reliable narrators. Thus, even later generations can have certainty about the miracles of past prophets.

Key Terms
المعجزة
العلم الضروري
التواتر
صدق المدعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that miracles are merely extraordinary events that do not constitute definitive proof.
Correction: This example shows that miracles produce necessary certainty (al-ʿilm al-ḍarūrī), not just probability.

Checkpoint

A) That the king speaks a certain phrase
B) That the king changes his habit by rising and sitting three times
C) That the king gives him a royal seal
D) That the king appears in a dream

Key Takeaway
A miracle, like the king's extraordinary act, gives necessary certain knowledge that the claimant is truthful, and this certainty is preserved through mutawātir transmission.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of the miracles of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) — like the splitting of the moon — do you feel the same level of certainty as if you had seen it yourself? This lesson says tawatur gives that certainty. What would change in your daily life if you truly internalised that certainty?
?
The king breaking his habit was enough for the group to know the claimant was truthful. Has there ever been a time when you demanded an extraordinary sign from Allah before obeying? This lesson shows that the miracles already given are sufficient. Will you commit to trusting in the proofs that have reached you through tawatur?
?

The Obligation of Tabligh (Delivery) for Prophets
Defines tabligh as delivering divine commands and proves its obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of tablīgh as a prophetic attribute and the scriptural evidence that establishes it as an obligation.

Core Idea
Prophets are obligated to deliver every divine command without exception.

Prophets are not merely recipients of revelation; they are also its transmitters. This passage defines the prophetic attribute of tablīgh—the duty to convey Allah's commands. It then provides two qur’ānic proofs that establish this obligation as essential to the office of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Start by reading the passage's clear definition of tablīgh: conveying the rulings to the people.
2
Examine the primary proof
Notice how the command in verse 5:67 ('Deliver what has been sent down to you') is treated as an obligation, supported by the doctrine of prophetic infallibility.
The command implies obligation (al-amr lil-wujūb).
3
See the secondary proof
Reflect on how the description of prophets as 'bearers of good news and warners' logically requires tablīgh.
This is from verse 4:165.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثاً : التبليغ (والتبليغ) أي : إيصال الأحكام التي أمروا بتبليغها إلى المرسل إليهم، إذ هم مأمورون بالتبليغ قال تعالى : يَا أَيُّهَا الرَّسُولُ بَلِّغْ مَا أُنزِلَ إِلَيْكَ مِن رَّبِّكَ وَإِن لَّمْ تَفْعَلْ فَمَا بَلَّغْتَ رِسَالَتَهُ (١)، والأمر للوجوب، وقد تقدَّم أنَّهم لا يخونون الله تعالى بفعل منهي عنه . وما ثبت له عليه الصَّلاة والسَّلام يثبتُ لهم، وقال تعالى: رُسُلًا مُبَشِّرِينَ وَمُنذِرِينَ (٢) ، ولا يتمُّ التبشير والإنذار إلا بالتبليغ .
Third: al-tablīgh (delivery). (And al-tablīgh) means: conveying the rulings which they were commanded to deliver to those to whom they were sent, for they are commanded to deliver. Allah Most High said: 'O Messenger, deliver what has been sent down to you from your Lord; if you do not, then you have not delivered His message' (1), and the command is for obligation. And it has preceded that they do not betray Allah Most High by performing a prohibited act. And whatever is established for him (peace and blessings be upon him) is established for them. And Allah Most High said: 'Messengers as bearers of good news and warners' (2), and the bearing of good news and warning is not completed except by delivery.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage defines and proves the prophetic attribute of tablīgh, i.e., the obligation to deliver the divine message. The definition: tablīgh is conveying the rulings that prophets were commanded to communicate to their respective communities. The proof of its obligation is the Qur'anic verse from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:67), which contains an explicit command (amr) to deliver, and the default legal status of a command is obligation (wujūb). Moreover, the author reminds the reader that prophets are infallible (ʿiṣma) and do not betray God by committing prohibited acts; hence, they necessarily fulfill this obligation. The passage also notes that what is established for Muhammad (peace be upon him) in terms of obligation applies to all prophets. Finally, another verse (Surah al-Nisa' 4:165) describes prophets as 'bearers of good news and warners,' which cannot be realized without delivering the message. Thus, tablīgh is an essential attribute of prophethood.

Key Terms
التبليغ (al-tablīgh)
إيصال الأحكام (īṣāl al-aḥkām)
الأمر للوجوب (al-amr lil-wujūb)
مبشرين ومنذرين (mubashshirīn wa mundhirīn)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets could choose not to deliver some parts of the divine message.
Correction: The passage proves that delivery is an obligation; withholding any part would be betrayal (khayanah), which prophets are infallibly protected from doing.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of tablīgh?
A) Performing miracles to prove prophethood
B) Conveying the divine rulings to the people
C) Interceding for the community on Judgment Day
D) Teaching the inner meanings of the scripture

Key Takeaway
Tablīgh is an essential prophetic attribute, proven by the Qur’ānic command and the very purpose of sending prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Prophets were commanded to deliver Allah's message fully, without hesitation. Is there a truth from Allah that you know but have been silent about because you fear someone's reaction? Will you commit to speaking it, even if it costs you comfort?
?
The verse warns: 'If you do not, then you have not delivered His message.' Are you fulfilling the duty of conveying what you know of Allah's commands to those around you—your family, friends, or community—or are you leaving it undone?
?
Prophets delivered despite opposition and personal cost. Is there a sin or wrong you tolerate in your own life because you have not 'delivered' the truth of Allah's command to your own soul? What command are you neglecting to obey today?

The Requirement of Intelligence (Fatana) in Prophets
Sanusi defines fatana and provides three proofs for its necessity in prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets must possess exceptional intelligence (fatana) and the three proofs used to establish this.

Core Idea
Prophethood demands the highest intellect — no dull mind can guide.

After discussing prophetic attributes like infallibility and truthfulness, Sanusi now turns to intelligence (fatana). He defines it as sharpness of mind and presents three compelling arguments for why prophets must be exceptionally intelligent. This passage shows that intellectual excellence is not optional but integral to their mission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to understand the overall argument.
Notice the three proofs are introduced with 'because' (li-anna).
2
Understand the definition of fatana
Fatana is defined as sharpness of mind and quick-wittedness. Identify the key terms in Arabic.
3
Analyze the three proofs
List the three reasons why prophets cannot be dull-witted. Think about how each reason connects to the mission of prophethood.
The passage concludes that prophets must be from the most honorable in station.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رابعاً : الفطانة : (والفطانة)، بفتح الفاء، وهي حدة العقل وذكاؤه. فلا يجوز أن يكون الرَّسول ولا النّبيُّ مُغفّلاً أو أبله أو بليداً ؛ لأنَّهم أُرسلوا لإقامة الحُجَج وإبطال شُبه المجادلين، ولا يكون ذلك من مُغفَّل ولا أبله ولأنَّا مأمورون بالاقتداء بهم في الأقوال والأفعال، والمقتدى به لا يكون بليداً ، ولأنَّ البَلادة صفةُ نَقْص تُخِلُّ بمنصبهم الشَّريف، ومن ذلك يعلم أنَّهم لا يكونون إلا من أشرف بمنصبهم الشَّريف
Fourth: al-faṭāna (intelligence). And al-faṭāna, with the opening of the fā', is sharpness of mind and its quick-wittedness. So it is not permissible that the messenger or the prophet be heedless, or a fool, or dull-witted; because they were sent to establish proofs and invalidate the doubts of disputants, and that cannot be from a heedless or a fool. And because we are commanded to follow them in statements and actions, and the one followed cannot be dull-witted. And because dull-wittedness is a deficiency that undermines their noble station. And from that it is known that they are only from the most honorable in their noble station.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage defines and argues for the necessity of the prophetic attribute of faṭāna, which means sharpness of intellect and quick-wittedness. The author begins with the lexical definition: the word is pronounced with a fatha on the fā', and it means keenness of mind and intelligence. Then he states the ruling: it is not permissible (lā yajūz) for a messenger or prophet to be either heedless, a fool, or dull-witted. Three proofs are given. First, prophets were sent to establish proofs (ḥujaj) against falsehood and to refute the doubts of opponents; this task requires acute intelligence, not heedlessness or foolishness. Second, Muslims are commanded to follow the prophets in their sayings and actions, and a dull-witted person is unsuitable as a role model. Third, dull-wittedness is a defect that would detract from the prophets' high status. The conclusion follows necessarily: prophets must be of the noblest intellect and highest station. Note that the passage ends mid-sentence at the page break, but the core argument is complete.

Key Terms
الفطانة (al-faṭāna)
حدة العقل (ḥiddat al-ʿaql)
ذكاء (dhakāʾ)
مغفل (mghaffal)
أبله (ablah)
بليد (balīd)
إقامة الحجج (iqāmat al-ḥujaj)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that prophets need not be exceptionally intelligent, since they receive divine guidance.
Correction: This passage shows that intelligence is necessary because prophets must engage in debate, serve as role models, and uphold dignity.

Checkpoint

A) They are sent to establish proofs against disputants
B) They receive revelation directly from God
C) We are commanded to follow them in words and deeds
D) Dull-wittedness is a defect unworthy of their station

Key Takeaway
Prophets must possess the highest level of intelligence because their mission requires establishing proofs, serving as role models, and maintaining dignity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Prophet's ﷺ statements, do you approach them as requiring deep thought, or do you assume they are simple because you think you already understand? Will you commit to pondering each hadith with the seriousness it deserves?
?
The Prophet ﷺ was the most intelligent of people. Does your study of his sunnah reflect a desire to sharpen your own intellect, or have you been content with superficial knowledge? What one step will you take this week to deepen your understanding of his teachings?
?
If dullness in faith is a deficiency, where is your own mind dull? Are there areas of your belief or practice that you have not thought critically about? Will you ask a teacher or seek resources to overcome that dullness today?

The Obligation of Delivery (Tablīgh) for Messengers
Explanation of the third wajib of messengers: delivery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of al-tablīgh as a necessary attribute of messengers and its scriptural proofs.

Core Idea
Messengers must deliver all they are commanded — it is their essential duty.

In this lesson, we examine the third wajib attribute of messengers: delivering the message. The author defines it clearly and supports it with two Quranic verses. Understanding this attribute helps us appreciate the complete trustworthiness of prophets in conveying revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition and proof
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how tablīgh is defined as conveying rulings that messengers were commanded to deliver.
The definition is straightforward - it is the act of delivering the message.
2
Analyze the Quranic evidence
Consider verse 5:67, which commands the Prophet to deliver and warns that failure equals not conveying the message. The command form indicates obligation.
This verse is the primary textual proof for the obligation.
3
Connect to the broader purpose
Reflect on verse 4:165, which states messengers are sent as bearers of good news and warners. These roles cannot be fulfilled without delivery.
Delivery is essential to the prophetic mission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثاً : التبليغ
(والتبليغ ) أي : إيصال الأحكام التي أمروا بتبليغها إلى المرسل إليهم، إذ هم مأمورون بالتبليغ قال تعالى : يَتَأَيُّهَا الرَّسُولُ بَلَغَ مَا أُنزِلَ إلَيْكَ مِن رَّبِّكَ وَإِن لَّمْ تَفْعَلْ فَمَا بَلَغْتَ رِسَالَتَه (١)، والأمر للوجوب، وقد تقدَّم أنَّهم لا يخونون الله تعالى بفعل منهي عنه .
وما ثبت له عليه الصَّلاة والسَّلام يثبتُ لهم، وقال تعالى: رُسُلًا مُبَشِّرِينَ وَمُنذِرِينَ (٢) ، ولا يتمُّ التبشير والإنذار إلا بالتبليغ .
Third: Delivery (al-tablīgh). (Al-tablīgh) means conveying the rulings that they were commanded to deliver to those to whom they are sent, for they are commanded to deliver. He, exalted, says: 'O Messenger, convey that which has been sent down to you from your Lord, and if you do not, then you have not conveyed His message' (5:67). And the command indicates obligation. It has preceded that they do not betray Allah, exalted, by doing a forbidden act. And what is established for him (peace and blessings be upon him) is established for them. And He, exalted, says: 'Messengers as bearers of good tidings and warners' (4:165), and the bearing of good tidings and warning is not completed except by delivery.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage defines the third wajib (obligatory attribute) of messengers: al-tablīgh (delivery). It begins by defining tablīgh as conveying the rulings that the messengers were commanded to deliver to their communities. The author then provides textual proof: Qur'an 5:67, which commands the Prophet to deliver what has been revealed and warns that failure to do so is a failure to convey the message. The command form indicates obligation (wujūb). The author then connects this to the earlier established point that messengers do not betray Allah by committing prohibited acts, implying that delivery is obligatory and they fulfill it. Finally, he cites Qur'an 4:165, stating that messengers are sent as bearers of good news and warners, and these functions cannot be realized without delivery. Thus, tablīgh is essential to the prophetic mission.

Key Terms

الرسول
الوجوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think delivery is only for general commands, but it includes all rulings they are commanded to convey.
Correction: The passage defines tablīgh as conveying 'the rulings that they were commanded to deliver' without restriction, and the Quranic verse commands delivering 'that which has been sent down' entirely.

Checkpoint

A) Speaking eloquently to the people
B) Conveying the rulings they were commanded to deliver to those to whom they are sent
C) Performing miracles to prove prophethood
D) Teaching religious sciences

Key Takeaway
The obligation of tablīgh means messengers must convey every ruling they are commanded to deliver, as proven by Quranic command and the purpose of their mission.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Messengers were obligated to deliver even when it was hard. What is one difficult truth you need to communicate to someone you care about, and what is stopping you from doing it?
?
You are not a messenger, but you are commanded to enjoin good and forbid evil. How have you neglected this duty in your daily interactions? Commit to one specific action this week to convey a reminder or warning.

The Necessity of Intelligence (Fatāna) for Prophets
Explanation of the fourth wajib of messengers: intelligence and its proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why intelligence (al-fatāna) is an essential attribute for prophets and the rational proofs for its necessity.

Core Idea
Prophets must be intelligent because their mission requires sharp reasoning and persuasion.

This lesson explains the fourth wajib among the attributes of messengers: al-fatāna (intelligence). The author, al-Sāwī, defines it as sharpness of mind and cleverness, then provides three compelling arguments for why a prophet cannot be dull or heedless. Understanding this strengthens our appreciation of the prophetic role and the divine wisdom in selecting messengers.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
First, read the lexical definition of al-fatāna. Notice the phrase 'ḥiddat al-ʿaql wa-dhakā'uh' – sharpness of mind and cleverness.
2
Examine the three proofs
The passage offers three reasons why dullness is impermissible for prophets. Identify each one and understand its logic.
3
Appreciate the conclusion
The passage concludes that prophets are free from anything that detracts from murū'a (moral uprightness). Ponder how this relates to intelligence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رابعاً : الفطانة :
(والفطانة)، بفتح الفاء، وهي حدة العقل وذكاؤه.
فلا يجوز أن يكون الرَّسول ولا النّبيُّ مُغفّلاً أو أبله أو بليداً ؛ لأنَّهم أُرسلوا لإقامة الحُجَج وإبطال شُبه المجادلين، ولا يكون ذلك من مُغفَّل ولا أبله ولأنَّا مأمورون بالاقتداء بهم في الأقوال والأفعال، والمقتدى به لا يكون بليداً ، ولأنَّ البَلادة صفةُ نَقْص تُخِل ذلك يعلم أنَّهم لا يكونون إلا من أشرف بمنصبهم الشَّريف، ومن الناس؛ رجالاً ونساءً، إذ شأن دنيء الأصول أن تأنف النَّفس من اتباعه والاقتداء به ، ولذا كانوا مُنزَّهين عن كلِّ ما يُخِلُّ بالمروءة، وكلّ ما يؤدي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العليَّة عليهم صلوات الله وسلامه .
Fourth: Intelligence (al-fatāna). (Al-fatāna), with the fatha on the fa, is sharpness of mind and cleverness. So it is not permissible for a messenger or a prophet to be heedless, dull, or stupid. Because they were sent to establish proofs and invalidate the doubts of disputants—and that is not done by a heedless or dull person. And because we are commanded to follow them in sayings and actions, and the one followed cannot be stupid. And because dullness is a deficiency that detracts from their lofty station. From this it is known that they are only from the most noble of people, men and women, for the nature of lowly origins is that the soul refuses to follow and emulate them. Hence they are free from everything that detracts from moral uprightness (al-murū'a) and everything that leads to deficiency in their exalted ranks, may the blessings and peace of Allah be upon them.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth wajib: al-fatāna (intelligence). It first gives the lexical definition: sharpness of mind and cleverness. Then it provides three proofs for its necessity: (1) Messengers are sent to establish proofs and refute the doubts of opponents—a task impossible for a heedless or dull person. (2) We are commanded to follow them in word and deed, and the one being followed cannot be stupid. (3) Dullness is a deficiency incompatible with their lofty rank; moreover, they must be from the noblest backgrounds (lineage, gender) because people naturally disdain following those of low origin. The passage concludes that messengers are free from anything that compromises moral integrity (al-murū'a) or their high status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-fatāna means worldly cunning or cleverness in deceit.
Correction: Al-fatāna here refers to sharpness of intellect needed for establishing proofs and guiding people, not cunning.

Key Takeaway
Prophets must possess sharp intelligence (fatāna) because their mission demands establishing proofs, being followed, and maintaining a noble station free from deficiencies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Am I prepared to accept that his commands are the most intelligent path, even when they are difficult? What concrete step will I take this week to submit my mind to his guidance?

Impossible Attributes of Messengers and Logical Oppositions
Enumeration of opposites with logical analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four impossible attributes of messengers (the opposites of the wajibat) and the specific logical opposition each pair exhibits.

Core Idea
Opposites of prophetic attributes are not all alike: some are contradictions, some contraries.

Sanusi has already established the four necessary attributes of messengers. Now he turns to their opposites—the attributes that are impossible for prophets. But the relation between each wajib and its opposite is not uniform; some are logical opposites, others are positive contraries. This passage clarifies these distinctions, showing the precision of kalam reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four opposites
Read the passage and list the four attributes that are impossible for messengers, which are the opposites of the four wajibat (truthfulness, trustworthiness, delivery, intelligence).
These are betrayal (khiana), concealment (kitman), dullness (balada), and lying (kadhib) — though lying is implied as the opposite of truthfulness.
2
Understand the definition of 'opposite'
The passage explains that 'opposite' here means 'absolute contradictory' (al-munāfī). Notice how this general term is then specified into different types of logical opposition.
The author distinguishes between contradictory (thing and its negation) and contrary (two positive opposites).
3
Recognize the three types of logical opposition
The passage analyzes each pair: truth vs. lying (thing and its contrary), trust vs. betrayal (contraries), delivery vs. concealment and intelligence vs. dullness (thing and its contrary). Identify which type applies to each.
This analysis is crucial for understanding the nature of impossibility in prophetic attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان ما يستحيل في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام
(ويستحيل) في حقهم عليهم السلام (ضدها) أي: ضدُّ هذه الواجبات الأربعة المتقدّمة (عليهم) فيمتنع في حقهم:
أولاً : الخيانة
(1)
قال تعالى: (مِنْهُم مَّن قَصَصْنَا عَلَيْكَ وَمِنْهُم مَّن لَّمْ نَقْصُصْ عَلَيْكَ ) )
قوله : ( ضدُّها) : المراد بالضّدّ : مطلق المنافي؛ وذلك لأنَّ الكذب عدم مطابقة الخبر للواقع والخيانة فعل المحرَّمات والمكروهات والكتمان عدم الوفاء بما أمروا بتبليغه للخلق، وحينئذ فالتقابل بين الصدق والكذب تقابل الشَّيء والمساوي لنقيضه .
وأمَّا بين الأمانة والخيانة : فتقابل الضّدَّين؛ لأنَّه فسَّر الخيانة بالفعل وهو وجودي.
وأمَّا بين التبليغ والكتمان : فتقابل الشَّيء والمساوي لنقيضه، وكذا بين الفطانة والبلادة.
Explanation of what is impossible for them, peace and blessings be upon them. (And it is impossible) for them, peace be upon them, (their opposite), i.e., the opposite of these four aforementioned wajibat (for them). Thus it is impossible for them: First: Betrayal (al-khiyāna). (1) He, exalted, says: 'Among them are those We have related to you and among them are those We have not related to you' (40:78). His statement: 'their opposite' — what is meant by 'opposite' (al-ḍidd) is absolute contradictory (al-munāfī). That is because lying (al-kadhib) is the non‑correspondence of the report with reality, and betrayal (al-khiyāna) is the act of forbidden and disliked things, and concealment (al-kitmān) is the failure to fulfill what they were commanded to deliver to creation. Accordingly, the opposition between truth and lying is the opposition of a thing and its contrary (al-shay' wa al-musāwī li-naqīḍihi). As for trust and betrayal, it is the opposition of two contraries (ḍiddain), because betrayal is interpreted as an act, and it is positive (wujūdī). As for delivery and concealment, it is the opposition of a thing and its contrary, and similarly between intelligence and dullness.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage explains the impossible attributes (mustaḥīlāt) of messengers, which are the opposites of the four wajibat. It first states that the 'opposite' (al-ḍidd) here means 'absolute contradictory' (munāfī). Then it analyzes each pair: (1) Truth vs. lying: lying is the non‑correspondence of speech with reality, so the opposition is that between a thing and its contradictory (like existence and non‑existence). (2) Trustworthiness vs. betrayal: betrayal is a positive act (wujūdī), so the opposition is between two actual contraries (ḍiddain), not a thing and its negation. (3) Delivery vs. concealment: concealment is the failure to deliver, so it is a contradictory opposition. (4) Intelligence vs. dullness: similarly contradictory. The author also quotes a verse (40:78) to indicate that some messengers are not mentioned by name, but that does not affect the obligations. This lesson refines the theological understanding of how attributes relate to their opposites.

Key Terms
الخيانة
الكتمان
البلادة
التقابل
الضد
نقيض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All oppositions between a wajib and its opposite are of the same logical type (e.g., all are contradictory).
Correction: The passage shows that some oppositions are between a thing and its negation (privation) while others are between two positive contraries, as in the case of trustworthiness vs. betrayal.

Checkpoint
What type of opposition exists between al-amāna (trustworthiness) and al-khiyāna (betrayal)?
A) Contradictory (shay' wa naqīḍ)
B) Contrary (ḍiddain)
C) Something and its equal to a contradictory
D) Relational

Key Takeaway
In kalam, the logical relationship between a wajib and its opposite determines the nature of the impossibility, requiring precise analysis of each attribute pair.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that truthfulness is wajib for a messenger, and lying is its opposite. But in your daily speech, do you actively practice truthfulness as a positive quality, or are you merely avoiding obvious lies? What small compromise with dishonesty have you accepted that you need to repent from today?
?
The lesson shows that betrayal is not just failing to be trustworthy, but a positive act of forbidden deeds. Look at your relationships—with Allah and with people. Where have you performed a 'positive act' of betrayal, doing something forbidden while convincing yourself it's just a minor failure? Name it now and commit to stopping it.
?
The messengers are protected from concealment—they deliver the whole message. But you know part of His message (the Quran and sunnah) and yet conceal it from others by your silence or laziness. What truth are you withholding from someone who needs to hear it, and when will you deliver it?

Why Betrayal is Impossible for Prophets
Al-Sawi explains why betrayal is impossible for prophets via analysis of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the basis for the impossibility of betrayal (khiyana) for prophets, through the analysis of their actions and intentions.

Core Idea
Prophets never perform merely permissible acts; their intentions elevate all actions.

Al-Sawi begins by examining the nature of prophetic actions. He argues that while acts in themselves can be obligatory, recommended, or permissible, when considered with their accidental qualities and the prophet's station, they are always either obligatory or recommended. Permissible acts only occur with an intention that redirects them to something sought, such as teaching. This analysis shows that betrayal, as a prohibited act, cannot occur from prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on prophetic actions
Read the Arabic passage from 'بفعل منهي عنه' to 'فكيف بهؤلاء السادة الكرام' and the first marginal note. Understand the distinction between the act in itself and its accidental qualities.
2
Identify the types of actions
The passage mentions wājib, mandūb, and mubāḥ. Note how the mubāḥ is transformed for prophets.
Compare with saints who also elevate mubāḥ acts.
3
Connect to impossibility of betrayal
Reflect on how this detailed analysis proves that betrayal, a prohibited act, cannot occur. The key is that prophets never engage in actions that are merely permissible or prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بفعل منهي عنه، إذ أفعالهم لا تخلو عن الواجب والمندوب والمباح، وهذا بالنَّظر إلى الفعل في حدّ ذاته، وأمَّا لو نظر إليه بحسب عوارضه فالحقُ أنَّ أفعالهم دائرة بين الواجب والمندوب لا غير، وأما المباحُ فلا يقع منهم كما يقع من غيرهم، بل لا يقعُ منهم إلا مصاحباً لنيَّةٍ تصرفه إلى كونه مطلوباً، وأقله قصد التشريع للغير، وذلك من باب التَّعليم، وناهيك به مرتبة .
وإذا كان بعض تابعيهم؛ كالأولياء لا تخلو أفعاله من الواجب والمندوب بصرف المباحات بالنيَّة الصَّالحة إلى المندوبات، كأن يصرف الأكل للتَّقوي على العبادة وإقامة البنية، والجماع لصون النَّفس عن الحرام وللنَّسل المطلوب، وغير ذلك، فكيف بهؤلاء السادة الكرام عليهم أفضل الصلاة والسَّلام .
ثانياً : وكذا يستحيل عليهم الكذب لما مرّ، ولقوله تعالى : (وَلَوْ نَقَولَ عَلَيْنَا بَعْضَ الْأَقَاوِيلِ لَأَخَذْنَا مِنْهُ بِالْيَمِينِ ثُمَّ لَقَطَعْنَا مِنْهُ الْوَتِينَ فَمَا مِنكُم مِنْ أَحَدٍ عَنْهُ حَجِرِينَ (١)
٤٥
ثالثاً : وكذا يستحيل عليهم كتمان شيء مما أُمروا بتبليغه، إذ كيف
قوله : (بفعل منهي عنه : الباء للتّصوير .
قوله : (لما مرَّ ) : أي : من الدَّليل العقلي.
وقوله : ( ولقوله تعالى . . . إلخ) : هذا هو الدليل النقلي . .
(۱) سورة الحاقة : (٤٤-٤٧).
By a prohibited act, because their actions are not free from the obligatory, the recommended, and the permissible. This is with consideration to the act in itself. As for considering it according to its accidental qualities, the truth is that their actions are confined to the obligatory and the recommended only. As for the permissible, it does not occur from them as it occurs from others. Rather, it only occurs from them accompanied by an intention that turns it into something sought, and the least of that is the intention of legislation for others, and that is from the category of teaching, and sufficient is that rank. And if some of their followers, like the saints, have actions not free from the obligatory and the recommended by turning permissible acts through good intention into recommended ones, such as directing eating for strength for worship and maintaining the body, and sexual intercourse for safeguarding oneself from the unlawful and for the desired progeny, and other things, then how about these noble masters, may the best prayer and peace be upon them. Secondly: likewise lying is impossible for them because of what has passed, and due to His saying the Most High: 'And if he had fabricated against Us some sayings, We would have seized him by the right hand, then We would have cut from him the aorta, and none of you could have withheld Us from him.' Thirdly: likewise concealment of something they were commanded to convey is impossible for them, because how... His saying: (by a prohibited act) the ba' is for picturing. His saying: (due to what has passed) meaning from the rational proof. And his saying: (and due to His saying the Most High... etc.) this is the transmitted proof. (1) Surah al-Haqqah: 44-47.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is a three-part argument proving that certain attributes are impossible for prophets. First, the author explains the impossibility of betrayal (al-khiyana) by analyzing the nature of prophetic actions. He says that when an act is considered in itself, it can be obligatory, recommended, or permissible. But when considering the accidental qualities and the high station of prophets, their actions are confined to the obligatory and recommended only. Permissible acts (mubah) do not occur from them as they do from ordinary people; rather, they always accompany an intention that redirects the act to being something desirable (matlub), such as the intention of legislation (tashri‘) for others. He then compares this to saints (awliya’) who also elevate their permissible acts to recommended ones through good intentions, such as eating for strength for worship or sexual intercourse for safeguarding from the unlawful and for progeny. If even saints can do this, then prophets certainly do it more perfectly. This shows that betrayal, which is a prohibited act, cannot occur from them. Second, the author states that lying is impossible for prophets, providing two proofs: a rational proof (al-dalil al-‘aqli) — 'due to what has passed' (لما مرّ), referring to earlier rational arguments — and a transmitted proof (al-dalil al-naqli) — the Quranic verse from Surah al-Haqqah (69:44-47) indicating that if the Prophet had fabricated sayings, Allah would have seized him and cut his aorta, and none could protect him. Third, the author begins to discuss the impossibility of concealment (al-kitman) but the text cuts off at 'because how...' The author also includes marginal notes explaining that 'bif‘li manhiyyin ‘anhu' the ba' is for depiction (al-taswir), and that 'lima marra' refers to the rational proof, and 'liqawlihi ta‘ala' is the transmitted proof. The lesson demonstrates the careful argumentation used to establish prophetic infallibility.

Key Terms
خيانة
واجب
مندوب
مباح
نية
تشريع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets can perform permissible acts like ordinary people without any special intention.
Correction: Prophets always accompany permissible acts with an intention that raises them to the level of sought acts, such as the intention of teaching.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the status of permissible (mubāḥ) actions when performed by prophets?
A) They remain permissible like for others
B) They are forbidden for prophets
C) They always occur with an intention that makes them sought (matlūb)
D) They never occur from prophets at all

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of betrayal for prophets is derived from the fact that their actions are always either obligatory or recommended, never merely permissible, and never prohibited.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform an act that is merely permissible, do you ever pause to consider that you could elevate it by intending to follow the Prophet's example or to teach others? What holds you back from doing so consistently?
?
If even saints elevate their permissible acts through good intentions, what does that reveal about the state of your own heart when you engage in daily activities? Are you content with the level of your intentions?
?
The Prophet never performed an act without an intention that sought something pleasing to Allah. Examine your last permissible action: what was your intention? Can you truthfully say it was for something sought (matlub) like a prophetic purpose? If not, what change will you make today?

The Impossibility of Lying and Concealment for Prophets
Al-Sawi proves lying and begins to prove concealment impossible for prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and scriptural proofs for the impossibility of lying (kidhb) and concealment (kitman) for prophets.

Core Idea
Lying and concealment are impossible for prophets, proven by reason and revelation.

After establishing the impossibility of betrayal, Al-Sawi turns to two other forms of infallibility: lying and concealment. He provides a rational proof (referring to earlier arguments) and a Quranic proof for lying, and begins the argument for concealment, though the text is incomplete. This lesson covers the second and third impossibilities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on lying and concealment
Read from 'ثانياً : وكذا يستحيل عليهم الكذب' to the end of the source passage, including the marginal notes.
2
Identify the two proofs for lying
The passage mentions a rational proof ('لما مرّ') and a transmitted proof (the Quranic verse from Surah al-Haqqah). Understand each proof.
The rational proof is not given here; it refers to previous arguments.
3
Examine the beginning of the concealment argument
The text starts the third impossibility but breaks off. Note the incomplete nature and consider why concealment would be impossible.

بفعل منهي عنه، إذ أفعالهم لا تخلو عن الواجب والمندوب والمباح، وهذا بالنَّظر إلى الفعل في حدّ ذاته، وأمَّا لو نظر إليه بحسب عوارضه فالحقُ أنَّ أفعالهم دائرة بين الواجب والمندوب لا غير، وأما المباحُ فلا يقع منهم كما يقع من غيرهم، بل لا يقعُ منهم إلا مصاحباً لنيَّةٍ تصرفه إلى كونه مطلوباً، وأقله قصد التشريع للغير، وذلك من باب التَّعليم، وناهيك به مرتبة .
وإذا كان بعض تابعيهم؛ كالأولياء لا تخلو أفعاله من الواجب والمندوب بصرف المباحات بالنيَّة الصَّالحة إلى المندوبات، كأن يصرف الأكل للتَّقوي على العبادة وإقامة البنية، والجماع لصون النَّفس عن الحرام وللنَّسل المطلوب، وغير ذلك، فكيف بهؤلاء السادة الكرام عليهم أفضل الصلاة والسَّلام .
ثانياً : وكذا يستحيل عليهم الكذب لما مرّ، ولقوله تعالى : (وَلَوْ نَقَولَ عَلَيْنَا بَعْضَ الْأَقَاوِيلِ لَأَخَذْنَا مِنْهُ بِالْيَمِينِ ثُمَّ لَقَطَعْنَا مِنْهُ الْوَتِينَ فَمَا مِنكُم مِنْ أَحَدٍ عَنْهُ حَجِرِينَ (١)
٤٥
ثالثاً : وكذا يستحيل عليهم كتمان شيء مما أُمروا بتبليغه، إذ كيف
قوله : (بفعل منهي عنه : الباء للتّصوير .
قوله : (لما مرَّ ) : أي : من الدَّليل العقلي.
وقوله : ( ولقوله تعالى . . . إلخ) : هذا هو الدليل النقلي . .
(۱) سورة الحاقة : (٤٤-٤٧).
By a prohibited act, because their actions are not free from the obligatory, the recommended, and the permissible. This is with consideration to the act in itself. As for considering it according to its accidental qualities, the truth is that their actions are confined to the obligatory and the recommended only. As for the permissible, it does not occur from them as it occurs from others. Rather, it only occurs from them accompanied by an intention that turns it into something sought, and the least of that is the intention of legislation for others, and that is from the category of teaching, and sufficient is that rank. And if some of their followers, like the saints, have actions not free from the obligatory and the recommended by turning permissible acts through good intention into recommended ones, such as directing eating for strength for worship and maintaining the body, and sexual intercourse for safeguarding oneself from the unlawful and for the desired progeny, and other things, then how about these noble masters, may the best prayer and peace be upon them. Secondly: likewise lying is impossible for them because of what has passed, and due to His saying the Most High: 'And if he had fabricated against Us some sayings, We would have seized him by the right hand, then We would have cut from him the aorta, and none of you could have withheld Us from him.' Thirdly: likewise concealment of something they were commanded to convey is impossible for them, because how... His saying: (by a prohibited act) the ba' is for picturing. His saying: (due to what has passed) meaning from the rational proof. And his saying: (and due to His saying the Most High... etc.) this is the transmitted proof. (1) Surah al-Haqqah: 44-47.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is a three-part argument proving that certain attributes are impossible for prophets. First, the author explains the impossibility of betrayal (al-khiyana) by analyzing the nature of prophetic actions. He says that when an act is considered in itself, it can be obligatory, recommended, or permissible. But when considering the accidental qualities and the high station of prophets, their actions are confined to the obligatory and recommended only. Permissible acts (mubah) do not occur from them as they do from ordinary people; rather, they always accompany an intention that redirects the act to being something desirable (matlub), such as the intention of legislation (tashri‘) for others. He then compares this to saints (awliya’) who also elevate their permissible acts to recommended ones through good intentions, such as eating for strength for worship or sexual intercourse for safeguarding from the unlawful and for progeny. If even saints can do this, then prophets certainly do it more perfectly. This shows that betrayal, which is a prohibited act, cannot occur from them. Second, the author states that lying is impossible for prophets, providing two proofs: a rational proof (al-dalil al-‘aqli) — 'due to what has passed' (لما مرّ), referring to earlier rational arguments — and a transmitted proof (al-dalil al-naqli) — the Quranic verse from Surah al-Haqqah (69:44-47) indicating that if the Prophet had fabricated sayings, Allah would have seized him and cut his aorta, and none could protect him. Third, the author begins to discuss the impossibility of concealment (al-kitman) but the text cuts off at 'because how...' The author also includes marginal notes explaining that 'bif‘li manhiyyin ‘anhu' the ba' is for depiction (al-taswir), and that 'lima marra' refers to the rational proof, and 'liqawlihi ta‘ala' is the transmitted proof. The lesson demonstrates the careful argumentation used to establish prophetic infallibility.

Key Terms
كذب
كتمان
دليل عقلي
دليل نقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets could potentially lie or conceal part of the message in times of difficulty.
Correction: The Quranic verse explicitly threatens severe punishment if the Prophet fabricated sayings, showing lying is impossible. Concealment would similarly break trust.

Checkpoint
Which Surah provides the transmitted proof for the impossibility of lying for prophets?
A) Surah al-Baqarah
B) Surah al-Haqqah
C) Surah al-Fatiha
D) Surah al-Ikhlas

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of lying for prophets is proven by both reason and revelation, while concealment is also impossible but the argument here is incomplete.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet ﷺ could not lie or conceal any part of the revelation, then every command he brought is absolutely true and binding. Which of his commands do you find hardest to fully accept, and what does that reveal about your own iman?
?
The Quran warns that if the Prophet had fabricated any saying, Allah would have seized him and cut his aorta. How does this divine guarantee of truthfulness make you re-evaluate your attitude toward the sunnah? Is there any sunnah you have been neglecting because of doubts?
?
The impossibility of concealment means the Prophet delivered the entire message without omission. Have you ever felt that some part of Islam is too difficult or embarrassing to follow? How will you respond now, knowing that it was never meant to be hidden?

Prophets' Acts Free from Forbidden and Directed to Mandub
Sawi explains prophets' permissible acts are directed to mandub by intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how prophets' permissible acts are always accompanied by an intention that elevates them to a recommended or obligatory status, distinguishing them from ordinary people.

Core Idea
Prophets never do anything without a purpose—every act is either obligatory or recommended.

In this lesson, we explore a key aspect of prophetic infallibility: the impossibility of committing forbidden acts. The author, al-Sawi, explains that while prophets' acts can be categorized as obligatory, recommended, or permissible in themselves, when considering their intentions and circumstances, they are always either obligatory or recommended. This shows the elevated nature of prophets and the intentionality behind every action.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the distinction between considering the act in itself and considering it with its accidentals.
The passage uses technical terms like wajib, mandub, and mubah.
2
Identify the two perspectives
The author presents two ways to view prophets' acts: (1) in themselves, which include three categories; (2) with regard to accidentals, which narrow to two. Find these in the text.
3
Understand the role of intention
Focus on how the permissible is redirected. The passage says even a permissible act always comes with an intention that makes it sought by God, such as teaching others.
The least intention is 'the intention of legislation for others'.
4
Reflect on the analogy with saints
The author compares prophets to 'awliya' (saints) who also redirect permissible acts through good intentions. This strengthens the argument.
Think about how this applies to daily actions like eating or marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما يستحيل في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام
بفعل منهي عنه، إذ أفعالهم لا تخلو عن الواجب والمندوب والمباح، وهذا بالنَّظر إلى الفعل في حدّ ذاته، وأمَّا لو نظر إليه بحسب عوارضه فالحقُ أنَّ أفعالهم دائرة بين الواجب والمندوب لا غير، وأما المباحُ فلا يقع منهم كما يقع من غيرهم، بل لا يقعُ منهم إلا مصاحباً لنيَّةٍ تصرفه إلى كونه مطلوباً، وأقله قصد التشريع للغير، وذلك من باب التَّعليم، وناهيك به مرتبة .
قوله : (بفعل منهي عنه : الباء للتّصوير .
وإذا كان بعض تابعيهم؛ كالأولياء لا تخلو أفعاله من الواجب والمندوب بصرف المباحات بالنيَّة الصَّالحة إلى المندوبات، كأن يصرف الأكل للتَّقوي على العبادة وإقامة البنية، والجماع لصون النَّفس عن الحرام وللنَّسل المطلوب، وغير ذلك، فكيف بهؤلاء السادة الكرام عليهم أفضل الصلاة والسَّلام .
What is impossible for them, peace and blessings be upon them: by a forbidden act, for their acts are not devoid of the obligatory, the recommended, and the permissible. This is with regard to the act in itself. But if one looks at it according to its accidentals, the truth is that their acts revolve between the obligatory and the recommended only. As for the permissible, it does not occur from them as it occurs from others. Rather, it occurs from them only accompanied by an intention that redirects it to being sought [by God], and the least of that is the intention of legislation for others, and that falls under teaching, and sufficient for you is that rank. And if some of their followers, like the saints, their acts are not devoid of the obligatory and the recommended by turning permissible things through good intentions into recommended acts, such as turning eating to gain strength for worship and building the body, and intercourse to protect oneself from the forbidden and for the desired offspring, and other things, then how [more so] with these noble masters, upon them the best of prayers and peace?
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the impossibility of prophets committing forbidden acts. The author begins by stating that prophets' acts are never devoid of three categories: obligatory (wajib), recommended (mandub), and permissible (mubah). This is when considering the act in itself. However, when considering their acts with respect to their accidental circumstances, the truth is that prophets' acts are only either obligatory or recommended; permissible acts do not occur from them as they occur from ordinary people. Instead, when a prophet performs an act that is intrinsically permissible, it is always accompanied by an intention that redirects it to something sought by God, such as the intention of legislation for others, which falls under teaching. The author then draws an analogy: if even the followers of prophets, such as saints (awliya), can turn permissible acts into recommended ones through good intentions—like eating for strength in worship or marriage for avoiding sin and having offspring—then how much more so do the prophets themselves act with such elevated intentions.

مندوب
مباح
نية
أولياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets can engage in permissible acts without any intention, just like ordinary people.
Correction: The passage explains that even their permissible acts are always directed to a higher purpose, such as teaching.

Checkpoint
According to Sawi, when considering the accidental circumstances of a prophet's act, what are the only two categories his acts can fall into?
A) Obligatory and permissible
B) Obligatory and recommended
C) Recommended and permissible
D) Permissible and forbidden

Key Takeaway
Prophets' permissible acts are never purposeless; they are always accompanied by an intention that elevates them to a recommended or obligatory status, demonstrating their perfect obedience and role as teachers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you eat your next meal, will you pause to set an intention—like gaining strength for worship or showing gratitude—as the prophets did? What needs to change in your mindset to make that a habit?
?
Are there permissible activities in your daily routine (e.g., sleep, work, conversation) that you have never considered offering to God? What specific intention could transform one of them into an act of worship starting tomorrow?
?
The prophets taught others even through their mundane acts. Look at your life today: is there someone you influence by your actions? If you realized they are watching, would you change anything? Commit to one small action you will do with the intention of teaching by example before the day ends.

The Impossibility of Lying for Prophets
Sawi asserts prophets cannot lie, citing rational proof and Quranic verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and textual evidence for why lying is impossible for prophets.

Core Idea
Prophets cannot lie; both reason and revelation confirm it.

This lesson examines a key doctrine of prophethood: that prophets are protected from lying. The author, al-Sawi, presents both a rational argument and a direct Quranic proof to establish this. By engaging with this passage, you will see how Islamic theology uses both intellect and scripture to defend prophetic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the dual evidence.
2
Identify the two proofs
Notice that the author explicitly mentions 'rational proof' and 'textual proof' from the Quran.
3
Reflect on why both are needed
Consider why theologians emphasize both reason and revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانياً : وكذا يستحيل عليهم الكذب لما مرّ، ولقوله تعالى : (وَلَوْ نَقَولَ عَلَيْنَا بَعْضَ الْأَقَاوِيلِ لَأَخَذْنَا مِنْهُ بِالْيَمِينِ ثُمَّ لَقَطَعْنَا مِنْهُ الْوَتِينَ فَمَا مِنكُم مِنْ أَحَدٍ عَنْهُ حَجِرِينَ) (١)
قوله : (لما مرَّ ) : أي : من الدَّليل العقلي.
وقوله : ( ولقوله تعالى . . . إلخ) : هذا هو الدليل النقلي . .
(۱) سورة الحاقة : (٤٤-٤٧).
Secondly: Likewise, lying is impossible for them due to what has passed, and because of His statement, exalted: 'And if he had made up about Us some [false] sayings, We would have seized him by the right hand; then We would have cut from him the aorta. And there is no one of you who could prevent it from him.' (1) His statement: 'due to what has passed' i.e., from the rational proof. And his statement: 'and because of His statement, exalted... etc.' This is the textual proof. (1) Surah Al-Haqqah: 44-47.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is a proof that lying is impossible for prophets. The author lists this as the second point. He first mentions the rational proof ('due to what has passed'), which presumably refers to an earlier argument that prophets must be truthful to be reliable. Then he provides a textual proof from the Quran (69:44-47), where Allah warns that if the Prophet Muhammad had fabricated any sayings about Allah, he would be severely punished. This shows that lying is impossible for prophets, as Allah would not allow it. The marginal note clarifies that 'due to what has passed' refers to the rational proof, and the Quranic verse is the textual (naqli) proof.

Key Takeaway
