Prophets and Concealment: Commanded vs. Permitted
Sawi explains the impossibility of prophets concealing commanded revelation and categorizes other matters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophets cannot conceal any part of the revelation they were commanded to deliver, and that some divine secrets are either to be concealed or shared only with select individuals.

Core Idea
Prophets must convey what commanded, but may conceal permitted secrets.

This passage addresses a subtle question: do prophets have any secrets? Sawi clarifies that prophets are utterly incapable of concealing any part of the revelation they were commanded to deliver. However, there are divine secrets they are commanded to conceal, and they may share some with select individuals like the four caliphs and Abu Huraira. A marginal note offers an alternative classification that reframes these categories.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic evidence
Begin with the opening Quranic proof (2:159) which curses those who conceal revealed guidance. Notice that this establishes a general principle, and prophets must be free from such a curse.
The verse is partially quoted; its message is clear.
2
Identify the main categories
The passage distinguishes matters commanded to be conveyed (which prophets must deliver fully) from other matters. Among the latter, some are optional and some must be concealed.
Look for the terms 'خُيّر' (choice) and 'يجب كتمانه' (must conceal).
3
Examine the special subcategory
Within matters that must be concealed, there is a subset that prophets were permitted to convey to specific individuals, such as the four caliphs and Abu Huraira. These secrets later circulate among saints.
This shows that not all concealed knowledge is absolutely hidden.
4
Consider the alternative classification
The marginal note presents a different view: some scholars treat the permitted-to-individuals category as part of the 'choice' category, resulting in three overall categories: commanded to convey, commanded to conceal, and choice.
Compare this with the two-category division in the main text.
5
Reflect on the overall doctrine
The key point is that prophets are infallible in delivering revelation, but may have knowledge that is not for public dissemination. This balances their mission with divine wisdom.
This lesson connects to the broader topic of prophetic infallibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثاً : وكذا يستحيل عليهم كتمان شيء مما أُمروا بتبليغه، إذ كيف يقع منهم الكتمان، وهو ملعون صاحبه بنص قوله تعالى : (إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يَكْتُمُونَ مَا أَنزَلْنَا مِنَ الْبَيِّنَتِ وَالْهُدَى مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا بَيْنَهُ لِلنَّاسِ فِي الْكِتَبِ... الآية (1) .
وأمَّا ما لم يؤمروا بتبليغه ؛ فبعضُه يُخيَّرون في تبليغه، وهو ما لم يؤمروا بعدم تبليغه، وبعضُه يجب كتمانه، وهو ما أمروا بكتمانه؛ كبعض الأسرار الإلهية، وبعضُ هذا القسم أُذن لهم في إيصاله لبعض الأفراد ؛ كالخلفاء الأربعة وكأبي هريرة ، وهذه الأسرار هي المتداولة بين الأولياء.
قوله : (وبعض هذا القسم أذن لهم في إيصاله . . . إلخ) : وبعض العلماء يجعل هذا من القسم المخيَّر فيه فتكون الأقسام ثلاثة : ما أمروا بتبليغه لم يكتموا منه حرفاً، وما أمروا بكتمانه لم يبلغوا منه حرفاً، وما خيروا فيه بلغوا البعض وكتموا البعض، وما بلغوه منه هو الأسرار الإلهية السارية في الأولياء، وهذا هو الظاهر .
Thirdly: Likewise, concealment of anything they were commanded to convey is impossible for them, for how could concealment occur from them, while its companion is cursed by the text of His statement, exalted: 'Indeed, those who conceal what We sent down of clear proofs and guidance after We made it clear for the people in the Scripture...' (1) As for what they were not commanded to convey, some of it they are given a choice in conveying, which is what they were not commanded not to convey, and some of it its concealment is obligatory, which is what they were commanded to conceal, like some divine secrets, and some of this category they were permitted to convey to certain individuals, like the four caliphs and Abu Huraira, and these secrets are those circulated among the saints. His statement: 'and some of this category they were permitted to convey... etc.' Some scholars make this part of the category in which they have a choice, so there are three categories: what they were commanded to convey—they did not conceal a letter of it; what they were commanded to conceal—they did not convey a letter of it; and what they had a choice in—they conveyed some and concealed some, and what they conveyed of it are the divine secrets flowing among the saints, and this is apparent.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is a classification and proof regarding the impossibility of prophets concealing what they were commanded to convey. The author begins with a Quranic proof (2:159) that those who conceal clear proofs and guidance are cursed, so prophets cannot be such. Then he explains that matters not commanded to be conveyed fall into categories: (1) those they are given a choice in conveying, (2) those they must conceal (like divine secrets), and (3) a subset of the latter for which they are permitted to convey to specific individuals (e.g., the four caliphs and Abu Huraira). The marginal note adds that some scholars consider the third category as part of the category of choice, resulting in three overall categories: commanded to convey (none concealed), commanded to conceal (none conveyed), and choice (some conveyed, some concealed). The secrets conveyed are those that circulate among saints.

Key Terms
كتمان
تبليغ
أسرار إلهية
خلفاء أربعة
أبو هريرة
أولياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets must convey absolutely everything they know without exception.
Correction: They must convey all revelation commanded, but some divine secrets they are commanded to conceal, and they may choose to convey some to select individuals.

Checkpoint
According to the marginal note, how many categories are there regarding what prophets are commanded to convey and not convey?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Prophets are infallible in conveying revelation, but may conceal or share divine secrets only as permitted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you convey knowledge about Islam, are you careful to transmit exactly what Allah has commanded, without adding your own opinions or hiding uncomfortable truths? The curse upon those who conceal clear proofs (2:159) is severe—does this weigh on your conscience when you teach or speak about religion?
?
Prophet Muhammad (s) was commanded to conceal certain divine secrets and only shared them with select companions like Abu Huraira. Are there matters Allah has entrusted you to keep secret, and are you faithful to that trust, or do you share them carelessly?
?
The passage shows that prophets have discretion in some matters—they may choose to convey or conceal. In your daily interactions, do you recognize which matters you are free to speak about and which you must keep silent? How do you decide, and what guides your choice?

Prophets Are Free from Mental Defects and Permissible Human Attributes
Sawi enumerates impossible mental defects and conditions for permissible human attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which mental defects are impossible for prophets and what human attributes are permissible for them without diminishing their rank.

Core Idea
Prophets can have ordinary human attributes, but never mental defects that degrade their mission.

The passage establishes two key boundaries for prophets: they are protected from specific mental defects that would undermine their message, yet they are still human and can experience permissible human conditions. Knowing these boundaries helps us avoid both exaggeration and undue criticism of prophets.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three impossible mental defects
Read the Arabic and translation to find the three mental defects that Sawi says are impossible for prophets. Why would these be incompatible with prophethood?
These defects would prevent prophets from conveying revelation accurately.
2
Understand the rule for permissible human attributes
Sawi states that any human attribute (arad bashari) is permissible provided it does not lower their high rank. Note the three conditions he gives.
The list of conditions may be incomplete in the source text.
3
Reflect on the balance between humanity and perfection
Consider how this teaching protects both the human nature of prophets and their exalted status. Why is it important that prophets can experience ordinary human conditions?
This balances the belief in their sinlessness with their full humanity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رابعاً : وكذا يستحيل عليهم البلاهة والغفلة والبلادة.
بيان
ما يجوز في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام
( وجائز) عليهم كلُّ عَرَض بشريّ لا يؤدّي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العَليَّة، بألا يكون منهيّاً عنه ولا مباحاً مُزرياً، ولا مرضاً مُؤْمناً أو...
Fourthly: Likewise, idiocy, heedlessness, and dullness are impossible for them. Explanation of what is permissible for them, peace and blessings be upon them: (And permissible) for them is every human attribute that does not lead to a deficiency in their high ranks, by not being forbidden, nor a degrading permissible [act], nor a fatal or disfiguring disease, or...
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a statement of what is impossible and what is permissible for prophets. First, the author lists three mental defects as impossible for prophets: stupidity (balaha), heedlessness (ghafla), and dullness (balada). These would undermine their mission and credibility. Then, he explains what is permissible for them: any human characteristic (arad bashari) that does not diminish their high rank. This is specified by three conditions: it must not be forbidden, it must not be a degrading permissible act (i.e., socially degrading even if legally permissible), and it must not be a fatal or disfiguring disease. The passage cuts off, indicating that there are more conditions or examples, but the basic principle is clear: prophets can experience ordinary human attributes as long as they do not lower their status or contradict their perfection.

Key Terms
بلاهة
غفلة
بلادة
عرض بشري
مراتب عليّة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets are free from all human weaknesses and cannot experience any human condition.
Correction: This passage clarifies that prophets can experience permissible human attributes (e.g., fatigue, minor ailments) as long as these do not degrade their rank or involve sin.

Checkpoint
According to Sawi, which of the following is NOT among the mental defects impossible for prophets?
A) Idiocy (balaha)
B) Heedlessness (ghafla)
C) Forgetfulness (nisyan)
D) Dullness (balada)

Key Takeaway
Prophets are protected from mental defects that would hinder their mission, but they can experience permissible human attributes that do not lower their rank.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself heedless (ghafla) in your worship, do you realize that you are displaying an attribute that is impossible for the prophets? What specific step will you take today to cultivate greater presence of mind in your prayers?
?
The prophets are free from dullness (balada) — spiritual and mental sluggishness. In what area of your life have you been mentally lazy when it comes to seeking the truth? What truth have you been avoiding, and what will you do about it this week?
?
If even a ‘permissible’ act that is socially degrading is not fit for a prophet, what does that say about your own choices? Is there a lawful habit in your life that actually lowers your dignity as a servant of Allah? Name it and make a firm resolve to abandon it.

Three Categories of Prophetic Communication
Al-Sawi explains the division of what prophets are commanded or permitted to convey or conceal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of what prophets are commanded or permitted to convey or conceal, and how scholars classify divine secrets.

Core Idea
Prophets are not free to disclose all knowledge; they follow divine command in conveying or concealing.

Al-Sawi delves into a nuanced classification of prophetic communication. He explains that some matters are optional, some obligatory to conceal, and some permitted only to chosen individuals. This clarifies the role of prophets as conveyors of revelation while safeguarding divine secrets.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to grasp the overall classification before analyzing details.
Notice the initial division into what they are not commanded to convey.
2
Identify the three categories in the reclassification
Pay attention to the three categories mentioned: (1) commanded to convey, (2) commanded to conceal, (3) given a choice. Note how the third includes the permissibility to tell certain individuals.
This reclassification is the key point of the passage.
3
Consider the examples
Reflect on the examples of the four caliphs and Abu Hurayra, who were entrusted with divine secrets that later circulated among the awliya'.
This shows that some secrets are not for the general public.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this classification prevents the misunderstanding that prophets reveal everything they know, and how it upholds the sanctity of certain divine knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا ما لم يؤمروا بتبليغه ؛ فبعضُه يُخيَّرون في تبليغه، وهو ما لم يؤمروا بعدم تبليغه، وبعضُه يجب كتمانه، وهو ما أمروا بكتمانه؛ كبعض الأسرار الإلهية، وبعضُ هذا القسم أُذن لهم في إيصاله لبعض الأفراد؛ كالخلفاء الأربعة وكأبي هريرة، وهذه الأسرار هي المتداولة بين الأولياء. قوله : (وبعض هذا القسم أذن لهم في إيصاله . . . إلخ) : وبعض العلماء يجعل هذا من القسم المخيَّر فيه فتكون الأقسام ثلاثة : ما أمروا بتبليغه لم يكتموا منه حرفاً، وما أمروا بكتمانه لم يبلغوا منه حرفاً، وما خيروا فيه بلغوا البعض وكتموا البعض، وما بلغوه منه هو الأسرار الإلهية السارية في الأولياء، وهذا هو الظاهر .
As for that which they are not commanded to convey, some of it they are given a choice in conveying it, and that is what they are not commanded not to convey. And some of it they must conceal, and that is what they are commanded to conceal, such as some divine secrets. And some of this category they are permitted to deliver to certain individuals, such as the four caliphs and Abu Hurayra, and these are the secrets circulating among the awliya'. His statement: '(And some of this category they are permitted to deliver... etc.)': And some scholars make this part of the category in which they are given a choice, so the categories become three: what they are commanded to convey — they did not conceal a single letter of it; what they are commanded to conceal — they did not transmit a single letter of it; and what they are given a choice in — they conveyed some and concealed some. And what they conveyed of it is the divine secrets that permeate the awliya', and this is the apparent view.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the classifications of what prophets are required or permitted to communicate. It begins by dividing what they are not explicitly commanded to convey into two subcategories: that which they are given a choice to convey or not (so long as they were not instructed to withhold it), and that which they must conceal because they were commanded to keep it secret, such as certain divine secrets. Then it notes a third subcategory within the second: some secrets they were permitted to disclose to specific individuals like the four caliphs and Abu Hurayra, and these are the secrets that later circulate among saints (awliya'). Then the author quotes his own previous words and adds that some scholars reclassify this third subcategory into the first (i.e., optional), resulting in three categories: (1) what they were commanded to convey — they never concealed a letter of it; (2) what they were commanded to conceal — they never transmitted a letter of it; and (3) what they were given a choice in — they conveyed some and concealed some. The conveyed portion of the third is exactly the divine secrets that permeate the awliya', and this is considered the apparent position.

Key Terms
تبليغ
كتمان
أسرار إلهية
أولياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets are free to reveal all they know.
Correction: Some matters are divinely commanded to be kept secret, and prophets must not disclose them. They follow divine command in what they convey or conceal.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on secrets that prophets were commanded to conceal?
A) They are free to convey them if they wish
B) They must conceal them entirely
C) They must convey them to everyone
D) They are only allowed to reveal them to the awliya'

Key Takeaway
Prophets strictly follow divine command in communication; some secrets are reserved for specific individuals and circulate among the awliya'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a teaching in Islam that seems to limit access to certain knowledge (like the secrets mentioned here), does your heart respond with trust in Allah's wisdom or resentment at not being included? What does that reveal about your faith in divine justice?
?
Consider a secret or insight about yourself that you have been commanded by Allah to keep private (e.g., a sin you repented from, a blessing meant for you alone). Are you faithful to that command, or do you feel the urge to share it for praise or sympathy? How can this lesson strengthen your discipline?
?
The prophets conveyed only what they were commanded — not more, not less. In your daily life, are you equally careful to speak only what Allah has permitted and to remain silent on what He has not? What specific situation today will you apply this to?

Permissible Human Experiences for Prophets and Their Benefits
Al-Sawi defines permissible human attributes for prophets and lists three benefits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what human attributes are permissible for prophets and why they experience them despite their high rank.

Core Idea
Prophets fully experience humanity—for reward, legislation, and consolation.

Al-Sawi now addresses a crucial aspect of prophetic theology: the humanity of prophets. While they are sinless and honored, they are not disembodied spirits. This passage defines the boundaries of their human experiences and reveals the wisdom behind them, showing that even their mundane or difficult moments serve divine purposes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall content.
Notice the structure: definition, categories, then benefits.
2
Identify the three categories of permissible attributes
Find the three types of human attributes Al-Sawi lists: indispensable, dispensable, and non-repulsive illnesses. Understand what each includes.
The exclusion criteria are also important.
3
Examine the three benefits
Read the three benefits: reward elevation, legislation, and consolation. Notice how each is justified with reference to divine wisdom and prophetic practice.
Legislation example: forgetfulness in prayer.
4
Understand the clarification on marriage
Read the gloss on 'marriage' (النكاح) and note the conditions: lawful intercourse, with free Muslim women through contract.
This shows the permissibility of marital relations for prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( وجائز) عليهم كلُّ عَرَض بشريّ لا يؤدّي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العَليَّة، بألا يكون منهيّاً عنه ولا مباحاً مُزرياً، ولا مرضاً مُؤْمناً أو تعافه النَّفس؛ كالجُذام والبَرَص، سواء كان مما لا يستغنى عنه عادة، (كالأكل والشرب والنّوم، أم كان ممّا يستغنى عنه كأكل الفواكه والنكاح، أو كان من الأمراض غير المُزمنة وغير المنفّرة، فكلُّ ذلك جائز في حقهم عليهم الصّلاة والسّلام. ولا تخلو هذه الأعراض النازلة بهم من فوائد : - كتعظيم أجورهم، وعُلوّ مراتبهم عند الله تعالى، والله تعالى وإن كان قادراً على أن يفعل بهم ذلك من غير ابتلاء ومشقة تحصل لهم، إلَّا أنَّ حكمته تعالى اقتضت ترتب ذلك على الابتلاء، لا يُسأل عما يفعل . - وكالتشريع، كما عرفنا أحكام السَّهو في الصَّلاة من سهوه، وكيف تؤدَّى الصّلاة في حال المرض والخوف من فعله عليه الصلاة والسلام حال ما ذكر ودلالة الفعل أقوى من دلالة القول . - وكالتّسلّي بأحوالهم إذا نزل بنا ما نزل بهم. قوله : (والنكاح) : المراد به الجماع في الحل أعم من أن يكون بعقد أو ملك يمين، لكن بقيد العقد بالمسلمات الحرائر .
(And permissible) for them is every human attribute that does not lead to a deficiency in their lofty ranks, provided it is not prohibited nor a degrading permissible act, nor a fatal or repulsive disease, such as leprosy and vitiligo. Whether it is something that is normally indispensable (like eating, drinking, and sleep), or something dispensable like eating fruits and marriage (sexual intercourse), or non-chronic and non-repulsive illnesses — all of that is permissible in their regard (peace be upon them). And these attributes that befall them are not devoid of benefits: — To magnify their rewards and elevate their ranks with Allah Almighty. Although Allah is able to do that for them without tribulation and hardship, His wisdom necessitated that this be contingent upon tribulation; He is not asked about what He does. — And for legislation, as we learned the rules of forgetfulness in prayer from his forgetfulness, and how prayer is performed during illness and fear from his action (peace be upon him) in those situations; and the indication of action is stronger than the indication of speech. — And for consolation in our situations when what befell them befalls us. His statement: '(and marriage)': By that is meant lawful intercourse, whether by contract or by ownership of the right hand, but with the condition of contract with free Muslim women.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage defines what human attributes are permissible for prophets and enumerates their benefits. It begins by stating that every human attribute (عرض بشري) is permissible for prophets as long as it does not diminish their high rank. This excludes prohibited acts, degrading permissible acts, fatal or repulsive diseases like leprosy and vitiligo. Then it categorizes these permissible attributes into three types: those normally indispensable (eating, drinking, sleep), those dispensable but permissible (eating fruits, marriage), and non-chronic, non-repulsive illnesses. All are allowed. Then it lists three benefits: (1) increasing their reward and rank with Allah, even though Allah could grant these without hardship; His wisdom ties reward to tribulation. (2) Legislation — for example, the rules of forgetfulness in prayer were derived from the Prophet's own forgetfulness, and how to pray in sickness and fear from his actions; actions are stronger indicators than words. (3) Consolation for those experiencing similar trials. Then a gloss defines 'marriage' (النكاح) as lawful intercourse, whether by contract or slave ownership, but with the condition of contract with free Muslim women.

Key Terms

عرض بشري
فوائد
تشريع
تسلي
نكاح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets cannot have any human afflictions or needs; they are above all human experiences.
Correction: Prophets do experience permissible human attributes—including needs, dispensable acts, and non-repulsive illnesses—for higher purposes like reward elevation, legislation, and consolation.

Checkpoint

A) Magnifying their rewards and ranks
B) Providing legislation through their actions
C) Demonstrating that they are not human
D) Offering consolation to believers

Key Takeaway
Prophets experience permissible human attributes—including needs, dispensable acts, and non-repulsive illnesses—for the profound purposes of reward elevation, legal guidance, and believer consolation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial, do you immediately seek comfort, or do you pause to consider that Allah may be using that hardship to elevate your rank, just as He did with the prophets? What one attitude can you change today to embrace this truth?
?
The Prophet's forgetfulness in prayer became a source of legislation for the entire ummah. How might your own shortcomings—your slip-ups or moments of weakness—be transformed into lessons for others if you submit them to Allah? Will you commit to reflecting on at least one personal failure this week and asking Allah to turn it into a benefit for others?
?
Are you truly content with Allah's wisdom when He allows trials into your life, even though He could have given you the same reward without hardship? Or do you secretly wish for a easier path? What does your heart's response reveal about your trust in His plan, and what step will you take to align your will with His?

The Low Value of the World and the Lesson from Prophets' Hardships
Al-Sawi explains the low value of the world and the wisdom of prophets' hardships.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the world is worthless in Allah's sight and how reflecting on the prophets' hardships leads a believer to turn entirely to God.

Core Idea
The world is so worthless that even a disbeliever gets only a sip of water.

In this passage, Al-Sawi explains a profound spiritual truth: the world has no value to Allah. He cites a hadith about a mosquito's wing and then shows how considering the prophets' sufferings can transform a believer's heart. Let's read the source and see how he builds this lesson.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the main point.
Notice the hadith about the mosquito's wing.
2
Focus on the hadith
The hadith says if the world were worth a mosquito's wing, Allah would not give a disbeliever a sip of water. Reflect on its implication.
3
Consider the prophets' hardships
The passage lists afflictions of the prophets: illnesses, lack of wealth, harm from people. See how the intelligent person responds.
4
Understand the lexical notes
Al-Sawi explains key phrases: 'خسة قدرها' (meanness of its value) and 'العيشة المرضية' (the pleasing life). Note the grammar.
These notes clarify the meaning.
5
Connect to the afterlife
The passage ends with the believer seeing after death the outcome of the pleasing life. This ties worldly detachment to eternal reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكالتنبيه على حقارة الدُّنيا وخِسَّة قدرها عند الله تعالى، ولذا قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لو كانت الدُّنيا تَزِن عند الله جَناحَ بعوضة ما سقى الكافر منها جَرْعة ماء» (١) ، فإذا نظر العاقل في أحوالهم عليهم الصّلاة والسّلام من أمراض وأسقام وقلة مال، وأذيَّةِ الخلق لهم، علم أنّها لا قدر لها عند الله تعالى فأعرض عنها بقلبه بالكلية، وعلق قلبه بربّه في البكرة والعشيَّة إن كان ذا هِمَّة عَليَّة، حتى يرى إثر موته عاقبة هذه العيشة المَرْضِيَّة. قوله : (وخسَّة قدرها أي لأنَّ حلالها حساب، وحرامها عقاب. قوله : (جرعة ماء) : بضم الجيم وفتحها، والمعنى : لو كان للدُّنيا قيمة قليلة توازن جناح بعوضة، فضلاً عن كونها كثيرة ما سقى . . . إلخ . قوله : (العيشة المرضيّة مفعول ثان ،لـ يرى، والأوّل قوله : (عاقبة هذه) . (١) أخرجه الترمذي (۲۳۲۰)، والحاكم في المستدرك ) (٣٤١/٤) عن سهل بن سعد
And as a reminder of the lowliness of the world and its mean value in the sight of Allah Almighty, therefore he (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'If the world were worth in the sight of Allah a mosquito's wing, He would not give the disbeliever a sip of water' (1). So when the intelligent person considers their conditions (peace and blessings be upon them) of illnesses, diseases, lack of wealth, and the harm of the people to them, he knows that it has no value in the sight of Allah Almighty, so he turns away from it with his heart entirely, and attaches his heart to his Lord morning and evening, if he has a high aspiration, until he sees after his death the outcome of this pleasing life. His words: (and its meanness) meaning because its lawful (halal) is account, and its unlawful (haram) is punishment. His words: (a sip of water) with damm of jim and fatha, and the meaning: if the world had a small value equaling a mosquito's wing, let alone being abundant, He would not give... etc. His words: (the pleasing life) is the second object of 'he sees', and the first is his words: (the outcome of this). (1) Reported by al-Tirmidhi (2320) and al-Hakim in al-Mustadrak (4/341) from Sahl ibn Sa'd.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the wisdom behind mentioning the low value of the world and how the believer should reflect on the hardships of the prophets. The author begins by stating that the mention of the world's lowliness serves as a reminder. He quotes the hadith that if the world had any value to Allah, He would not give a disbeliever even a sip of water. Then he explains that when a person of intelligence considers the afflictions of the prophets—sickness, poverty, harm from people—they realize the world's worthlessness in Allah's sight, and thus they turn away from it completely, attaching their hearts to Allah alone. After explaining that, the author provides lexical notes on the phrases "خسَّة قدرها" (meanness of its value), "جرعة ماء" (sip of water), and "العيشة المرضيّة" (the pleasing life), explaining grammar and meaning. The passage concludes with the hadith citation.

Key Terms
حقارة الدنيا
خسة قدرها
العاقل
العيشة المرضية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The world has some value because God created it.
Correction: The passage shows that even a disbeliever gets only a sip of water, indicating utter worthlessness in Allah's sight.

Checkpoint

A) To discourage the believer from seeking worldly wealth.
B) To make the believer realize the world's worthlessness and turn to God.
C) To prove that prophets were poor.
D) To explain a hadith.

Key Takeaway
The world's worthlessness is proven by the hadith that even a disbeliever gets only a sip of water, and reflecting on prophets' hardships leads to turning to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you chase after worldly comforts, do you ever pause to consider that even a sip of water for a disbeliever is a sign of this world's worthlessness? What would it take for you to truly turn away from it in your heart?
?
The prophets suffered illnesses, poverty, and harm, yet they attached their hearts to Allah. Where is your heart attached right now—to fleeting things or to the Eternal? What specific attachment must you break today?
?
If the lawful of this world brings account and the unlawful brings punishment, are you willing to examine every bite you take and every coin you earn? Are you ready to live with the constant awareness of the Hereafter, not just as a concept but as the reality that shapes your every choice?

Permissible Degrading Acts and Prophets
Al-Sawi lists acts included under 'al-mubah al-muzri' and their prohibition for prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which acts are considered degrading for prophets and why they are forbidden.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from acts that lower their dignity, even if those acts are permissible for others.

Al-Sawi begins by distinguishing actions that are merely permissible but degrading from those that are human and allowed. He specifies that begging or accepting charity and eating publicly in the market are such degrading acts. This lesson explains why prophets are immune to these behaviors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the degrading acts
Read the passage to find the specific acts that Al-Sawi includes under 'al-mubah al-muzri'.
These are begging or accepting charity and eating in the market.
2
Understand the reasoning
Reflect on why these acts are considered degrading and thus forbidden for prophets, even though they are normally permissible.
3
Apply the rule to other contexts
Consider whether similar acts today might fall under this category and why prophets must avoid them to maintain their dignity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودخل في قولنا : المباح المزري سؤالُ الصَّدقة، بل قبولها، فلا يجوز عليهم، والأكل في السوق. ودخل في المرض المُزمن العمى والجنون ولو قل؛ لأنَّ شأنه أن يزمن، ولأنّه نقص، ولم يعم نبيٌّ قَطُّ، وما قيل: إنَّ شعيباً ل كان حصل لك فقر مثلاً أو مرض تسلى بما وقع للأنبياء قبلك ضريراً لا أصل له ، ويعقوبُ إنما حصلت له غشاوة وزالت . وأمَّا السَّهو : فيجوز في الأفعال كالسَّلام من ركعتين دون الأقوال، وأما نسيان الأحكام فلا يجوز عليهم قبل التَّبليغ، ويجوز بعده لحفظه بعده، ولوجوب ضبطه على المبلغ ليعمل به وليبلغه، ويجوز نسيان المنسوخ مطلقاً قبل التبليغ وبعده. واعلم أنّ ما جاز عليهم من الأعراض البشرية التي لا تؤدّي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العَليَّة، فإنَّما هو بحسب ظواهرهم فقط، وأما بواطنهم فهي معمورة بالأسرار الإلهيَّة، متعلّقة بحبّ خالق البريَّة، فلا يحصل منهم ضَجَر ولا شكوى ولا تأوه منها، بل لا يزيدهم منه إلا قرباً وحبّاً، بل هذه الحالة تكون في كثير من أمتهم، فكيف بهم عليهم الصلاة والسّلام . قوله :(وزالت) أي حين جاءه البشير بقميص يوسف، كما أخبر الله تعالى بقوله : فَارْتَدَّ بَصِيرًا ) (١)
And included in our statement: the permissible that degrades (al-mubah al-muzri) is begging for charity, rather accepting it, so it is not permissible for them, and eating in the market. And included in chronic illness (al-marad al-muzmin) is blindness and insanity, even if slight, because its nature is to be chronic, and because it is a deficiency, and no prophet has ever become blind, and what is said: that Shu'ayb was blind? He has no basis, and Ya'qub only had a covering and it was removed. As for forgetfulness (al-sahw), it is permissible in actions like the greeting from two rak'ahs, but not in statements. As for forgetting rulings (nisyan al-ahkam), it is not permissible for them before conveying, and it is permissible after conveying, for its preservation after it, and due to the obligation of the conveyor to memorize it to act by it and convey it. And it is permissible to forget abrogated (al-mansukh) absolutely, before conveying and after it. And know that whatever is allowed for them of human accidents that do not lead to deficiency in their high ranks, it is only according to their outward appearances, but their inner selves are filled with divine secrets, attached to the love of the Creator of creation, so they do not suffer from them any anxiety, complaint, or sigh, rather it only increases them in closeness and love, indeed this state occurs in many of their nation, so how about them (peace and blessings be upon them)? His words: (and it was removed) meaning when the bearer of good news came with Yusuf's shirt, as Allah Almighty informed in His words: "So he returned seeing" (12:96).
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage discusses what human imperfections are permissible for prophets. It begins by stating what is included under 'al-mubah al-muzri' (the permissible that degrades): begging or even accepting charity, and eating in the market—these are not permissible for prophets because they degrade their status. Then it discusses chronic illness (al-marad al-muzmin): blindness and insanity, even in a slight amount, are considered chronic because they tend to persist and constitute a deficiency. The author asserts that no prophet has ever been blind, refuting the claim that Shu'ayb was blind, and explains that Ya'qub only had a temporary covering of the eyes which was removed. Then it discusses forgetfulness (al-sahw): it is permissible in actions (like the Prophet's salam from two rak'ahs) but not in statements. Forgetting rulings (nisyan al-ahkam) is not permissible before conveying the message, but it is permissible after conveying because the conveying is preserved and the conveyor is required to memorize for the sake of transmission. Forgetting abrogated rulings is permissible in all cases. Then the author draws an important distinction: whatever human accidents are allowed for prophets are only outward; inwardly they are filled with divine secrets and love of God, and they do not feel distress or complaint; rather, these things increase them in closeness and love. This state is found even among many of their followers, so how much more so for the prophets. The footnote explains that Ya'qub's sight returned when the shirt of Yusuf came.

Key Terms
المباح المزري
سؤال الصدقة
قبول الصدقة
الأكل في السوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that prophets can engage in any permissible human act without restriction.
Correction: Al-Sawi clarifies that certain permissible acts are degrading and thus prohibited for prophets to maintain their dignity.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Sawi, which of the following is NOT permissible for prophets?
A) Eating in the market
B) Begging for charity
C) Accepting charity
D) All of the above are not permissible

Key Takeaway
Prophets are forbidden from engaging in acts that degrade their dignity, even if those acts are otherwise permissible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Prophets are forbidden from actions that degrade their dignity, even if permissible. Think of a habit you consider 'harmless' or 'just a small thing'—could it be lowering your dignity without you realizing it? What is one such habit you will commit to abandoning starting today?
?
The lesson includes 'accepting charity' as degrading for prophets. When you receive help from others, is your heart filled with honor in Allah or with dependence on people? How can you actively cultivate self-sufficiency and reliance on Allah alone, even in small matters?
?
You are not a prophet, but you carry the banner of Islam in your community. This lesson shows that dignity is part of that responsibility. What 'permissible' action are you currently doing that might reduce your honor in the eyes of others and thus tarnish the image of Muslims? Will you stop it this week? Write down your specific commitment.

Chronic Illness: Are Prophets Afflicted?
Al-Sawi discusses chronic illness and its prohibition for prophets, with examples of blindness and insanity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why chronic illnesses like blindness and insanity are considered deficiencies and why prophets are protected from them.

Core Idea
No prophet has ever suffered chronic blindness or insanity; these are considered deficiencies incompatible with prophethood.

The passage continues with another category: chronic illness. Al-Sawi discusses whether blindness and insanity can afflict prophets. He asserts that they are deficiencies and that no prophet has ever been blind, refuting baseless claims about Shu'ayb and explaining Ya'qub's temporary loss of sight. This lesson unpacks the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the category of chronic illness
Read the passage to see how Al-Sawi defines chronic illness (al-marad al-muzmin) and why it is impermissible for prophets.
2
Examine the examples: blindness and insanity
Note that even a slight amount of these conditions is considered chronic and thus not allowed.
Blindness and insanity are given as examples.
3
Analyze the refutation of Shu'ayb's blindness and Ya'qub's case
See how Al-Sawi dismisses the claim about Shu'ayb and explains that Ya'qub's loss of sight was temporary.

Source Text

?
When you look at the prophets' perfect bodies and minds, do you feel inadequate in your own imperfections? Does this lesson remind you that your chronic ailments are not deficiencies of worth, but trials with a temporary nature? How will you thank Allah for the covering He may remove?

Forgetfulness in Actions but Not Statements
Al-Sawi differentiates between permissible forgetfulness in actions and impermissible forgetfulness in statements for prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between permissible forgetfulness in actions and impermissible forgetfulness in statements for prophets.

Core Idea
Prophets may forget in actions but never in statements, as their speech must be perfectly reliable.

Al-Sawi now turns to the issue of forgetfulness (sahw). He draws a sharp distinction between actions and statements: forgetfulness in actions is permissible, as seen in the Prophet's salam from two rak'ahs, but forgetfulness in statements is not. This lesson explores the reasoning behind this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Learn the category of forgetfulness
Read the passage to see what forgetfulness (al-sahw) entails and its permissibility for prophets.
2
Understand the action vs statement distinction
Notice that forgetfulness is allowed in actions but not in statements. Reflect on why this distinction exists.
3
Reflect on the example of the Prophet's prayer
Consider the incident of the Prophet giving salam after two rak'ahs as a concrete example of permissible forgetfulness in action.
This is a well-known hadith.

Forgetting Rulings: Before and After Conveying
Al-Sawi explains the permissibility of prophets forgetting rulings after conveying, and the absolute permissibility of forgetting abrogated laws.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand when it is permissible for prophets to forget rulings, especially regarding abrogated laws.

Core Idea
Prophets cannot forget rulings before conveying them, but may forget after, and forgetting abrogated laws is always allowed.

The passage now addresses forgetting rulings (nisyan al-ahkam). Al-Sawi explains that prophets are protected from forgetting any ruling before they have communicated it to the people. However, after they have conveyed it, forgetting is permissible because the ruling is already preserved. Moreover, abrogated laws can be forgotten entirely. This lesson clarifies these important distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the timing of forgetting rulings
Read the passage to see the two conditions: before conveying and after conveying.
2
Differentiate between before and after conveying
Note that before conveying, forgetting is not allowed; after conveying, it is allowed.
3
Learn the rule for abrogated rulings
Observe that abrogated rulings (al-mansukh) can be forgotten at any time, without restriction.

Source Text

When is it permissible for a prophet to forget a religious ruling according to the passage?

Key Takeaway
Prophets are protected from forgetting rulings before conveying, but may forget after, especially abrogated ones.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat the teachings of the Prophet as so urgent that you commit them to memory and act on them immediately, or do you allow yourself to 'forget' what you have learned until it is too late? What would change if you viewed each ruling as something you must convey to yourself before you can forget it?
?
If abrogated rulings can be forgotten without consequence, what does that imply about your attachment to outdated practices or opinions? Are you holding onto anything that has been abrogated by clear evidence?
?
This lesson teaches that prophets are only protected from forgetting before conveying. Reflect on your own role as a conveyer of truth: Are you careful to memorize and deliver what you know accurately, or do you risk forgetting or distorting the message before it reaches others?

intermediate
5 min
Outward Imperfections, Inward Perfection
Al-Sawi explains that the human imperfections allowed for prophets are only outward, while their inner state is perfect and full of divine love.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that while prophets may experience outward human imperfections, their inner spiritual state remains perfect and filled with divine love.

Core Idea
Prophets' outward imperfections never affect their inward perfection and love for Allah.

The final part of the passage offers a profound insight: any human accidents allowed for prophets are only outward; their inner selves are utterly pure, filled with divine secrets and love. They experience no distress or complaint, but these states increase their closeness to Allah. This lesson explains this distinction and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the distinction between outward appearance and inner reality
Read the passage to see how Al-Sawi separates outward (zahir) from inward (batin) for prophets.
2
Understand that outward imperfections do not detract from inner perfection
Note that the inner self is filled with divine secrets and love, regardless of outward trials.
3
Reflect on the absence of distress and increase in love
Consider that prophets do not feel anxiety or complaint from outward hardships; instead, these increase their closeness and love for Allah.

ودخل في قولنا : المباح المزري سؤالُ الصَّدقة، بل قبولها، فلا يجوز عليهم، والأكل في السوق. ودخل في المرض المُزمن العمى والجنون ولو قل؛ لأنَّ شأنه أن يزمن، ولأنّه نقص، ولم يعم نبيٌّ قَطُّ، وما قيل: إنَّ شعيباً ل كان حصل لك فقر مثلاً أو مرض تسلى بما وقع للأنبياء قبلك ضريراً لا أصل له ، ويعقوبُ إنما حصلت له غشاوة وزالت . وأمَّا السَّهو : فيجوز في الأفعال كالسَّلام من ركعتين دون الأقوال، وأما نسيان الأحكام فلا يجوز عليهم قبل التَّبليغ، ويجوز بعده لحفظه بعده، ولوجوب ضبطه على المبلغ ليعمل به وليبلغه، ويجوز نسيان المنسوخ مطلقاً قبل التبليغ وبعده. واعلم أنّ ما جاز عليهم من الأعراض البشرية التي لا تؤدّي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العَليَّة، فإنَّما هو بحسب ظواهرهم فقط، وأما بواطنهم فهي معمورة بالأسرار الإلهيَّة، متعلّقة بحبّ خالق البريَّة، فلا يحصل منهم ضَجَر ولا شكوى ولا تأوه منها، بل لا يزيدهم منه إلا قرباً وحبّاً، بل هذه الحالة تكون في كثير من أمتهم، فكيف بهم عليهم الصلاة والسّلام . قوله :(وزالت) أي حين جاءه البشير بقميص يوسف، كما أخبر الله تعالى بقوله : فَارْتَدَّ بَصِيرًا ) (١)
And included in our statement: the permissible that degrades (al-mubah al-muzri) is begging for charity, rather accepting it, so it is not permissible for them, and eating in the market. And included in chronic illness (al-marad al-muzmin) is blindness and insanity, even if slight, because its nature is to be chronic, and because it is a deficiency, and no prophet has ever become blind, and what is said: that Shu'ayb was blind? He has no basis, and Ya'qub only had a covering and it was removed. As for forgetfulness (al-sahw), it is permissible in actions like the greeting from two rak'ahs, but not in statements. As for forgetting rulings (nisyan al-ahkam), it is not permissible for them before conveying, and it is permissible after conveying, for its preservation after it, and due to the obligation of the conveyor to memorize it to act by it and convey it. And it is permissible to forget abrogated (al-mansukh) absolutely, before conveying and after it. And know that whatever is allowed for them of human accidents that do not lead to deficiency in their high ranks, it is only according to their outward appearances, but their inner selves are filled with divine secrets, attached to the love of the Creator of creation, so they do not suffer from them any anxiety, complaint, or sigh, rather it only increases them in closeness and love, indeed this state occurs in many of their nation, so how about them (peace and blessings be upon them)? His words: (and it was removed) meaning when the bearer of good news came with Yusuf's shirt, as Allah Almighty informed in His words: "So he returned seeing" (12:96).
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage discusses what human imperfections are permissible for prophets. It begins by stating what is included under 'al-mubah al-muzri' (the permissible that degrades): begging or even accepting charity, and eating in the market—these are not permissible for prophets because they degrade their status. Then it discusses chronic illness (al-marad al-muzmin): blindness and insanity, even in a slight amount, are considered chronic because they tend to persist and constitute a deficiency. The author asserts that no prophet has ever been blind, refuting the claim that Shu'ayb was blind, and explains that Ya'qub only had a temporary covering of the eyes which was removed. Then it discusses forgetfulness (al-sahw): it is permissible in actions (like the Prophet's salam from two rak'ahs) but not in statements. Forgetting rulings (nisyan al-ahkam) is not permissible before conveying the message, but it is permissible after conveying because the conveying is preserved and the conveyor is required to memorize for the sake of transmission. Forgetting abrogated rulings is permissible in all cases. Then the author draws an important distinction: whatever human accidents are allowed for prophets are only outward; inwardly they are filled with divine secrets and love of God, and they do not feel distress or complaint; rather, these things increase them in closeness and love. This state is found even among many of their followers, so how much more so for the prophets. The footnote explains that Ya'qub's sight returned when the shirt of Yusuf came.

Sending Messengers: A Favor, Not an Obligation
Al-Sawi states the ruling on sending messengers and refutes two opposing sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that sending messengers is a favor and mercy from Allah, not an obligation upon Him, and how this refutes both the Mu'tazila and the Brahmanas.

Core Idea
Sending messengers is a gift, not a debt.

Al-Sawi clarifies a fundamental point about prophethood: sending messengers is not something Allah is obligated to do. It is a pure favor (tafaddul) and mercy. This straightforward statement immediately refutes two opposing extremes: the Mu'tazila, who claimed Allah must send messengers, and the Brahmanas, who denied it entirely. Let's examine the passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic carefully, then the translation. Notice the opening statement and the contrast with the Mu'tazila and Brahmanas.
2
Identify the two views being refuted
The Mu'tazila made it obligatory; the Brahmanas deemed it impossible. See how the passage addresses both.
3
Reflect on the meaning of 'favor and mercy'
Consider why calling it a 'favor' (tafaddul) and 'mercy' emphasizes Allah's generosity, not any obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكم إرسال الرسل إرسال الرّسل تفضّل ورحمة من الله ولَمَّا أوجبت المعتزلة إرسال الرُّسل بناءً على قاعدتهم، من وجوب الصَّلاح عليه تعالى، والأصلحُ في حقّ عبيده أن يُرسل إليهم الرُّسل لينبهوهم على ما يُنجيهم من المهالك وما يُوبقهم فيها، وأحاله السمنية والبراهمة قوله : ( والبراهمة) : نسبة لبرهام كبيرهم (١)
The ruling on sending messengers: Sending messengers is a favor (tafaddul) and mercy from Allah. When the Mu'tazila made it obligatory to send messengers, based on their principle of the obligation of what is beneficial (salāh) upon Him Almighty, and the most beneficial (aslah) for His servants is to send messengers to them to alert them to what saves them from destruction and what will cause them to perish in it, the Samaniyya and the Brahmana deemed it impossible. His words: (and the Brahmana) is a relation to Barham, their great one.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage addresses the theological ruling on sending messengers. It begins with the heading: 'The ruling on sending messengers' and states that it is a favor (tafaddul) and mercy from Allah, not an obligation upon Him. Then it contrasts the Mu'tazilite position: they made it obligatory based on their principle that God must do what is beneficial (salāh) and most beneficial (aslah) for His servants, so He must send messengers to warn them. On the other hand, the Samaniyya and the Brahmana (Hindu sects) deemed sending messengers impossible (ahāla). The footnote explains that 'al-Barahima' is a nisba to Barham, their great leader. The passage thus refutes both extremes: the Mu'tazila who make it obligatory, and the atheists who deny it altogether.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God is obligated to send messengers to guide people.
Correction: The passage states that sending messengers is a favor and mercy, not an obligation.

Checkpoint

A) Because it is a favor from God.
B) Based on their principle of the obligation of what is beneficial and most beneficial.
C) Because the Brahmanas did.
D) Because it is mentioned in the Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
Sending messengers is a favor and mercy from Allah, not an obligation, refuting both the Mu'tazila and the Brahmanas.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as though God owes you guidance, or do you receive every prophet and message as a mercy you never deserved? How many times this week have you thanked Allah for sending Muhammad ﷺ?
?
When you hear an Islamic ruling you dislike, does your heart instinctively question God's justice? Have you ever caught yourself demanding that God explain Himself—as if He must answer to your sense of fairness?
?
If sending messengers were truly an obligation upon God, you could demand it. But it is a favor. What would change in your obedience if you treated every revelation as an undeserved gift rather than a right?

Forgetfulness and Human Attributes in Prophets
Defines permissibility of forgetfulness and human traits in prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rulings on forgetfulness for prophets and the distinction between their outward human attributes and inward perfection.

Core Idea
Prophets are human outwardly but inwardly flawless and devoted.

This passage from al-Kharida clarifies what human traits are acceptable for prophets. It distinguishes between forgetfulness in actions (permissible) and forgetfulness in rulings (restricted), and explains that any human imperfection is only external—their inner state remains pure.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source once, then the translation. Notice the structure: it begins by addressing a false claim, then discusses types of forgetfulness, and finally the inward/outward distinction.
2
Identify the categories of forgetfulness
The passage lists three scenarios: forgetfulness in actions (permissible), forgetfulness in rulings before and after delivery, and forgetfulness of abrogated rulings. Note the conditions for each.
Pay attention to 'before delivery' vs 'after delivery' for rulings.
3
Reflect on the inward/outward distinction
The passage states that human attributes are only outward; inwardly prophets are filled with divine secrets. Consider how this preserves their rank while acknowledging their humanity.
This addresses a common misconception about prophetic perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكم إرسال الرسل ضريراً لا أصل له ، ويعقوبُ إنما حصلت له غشاوة وزالت . وأمَّا السَّهو : فيجوز في الأفعال كالسَّلام من ركعتين دون الأقوال، وأما نسيان الأحكام فلا يجوز عليهم قبل التَّبليغ، ويجوز بعده لحفظه بعده، ولوجوب ضبطه على المبلغ ليعمل به وليبلغه، ويجوز نسيان المنسوخ مطلقاً قبل التبليغ وبعده. واعلم أنّ ما جاز عليهم من الأعراض البشرية التي لا تؤدّي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العَليَّة، فإنَّما هو بحسب ظواهرهم فقط، وأما بواطنهم فهي معمورة بالأسرار الإلهيَّة، متعلّقة بحبّ خالق البريَّة، فلا يحصل منهم ضَجَر ولا شكوى ولا تأوه منها، بل لا يزيدهم منه إلا قرباً وحبّاً، بل هذه الحالة تكون في كثير من أمتهم، فكيف بهم عليهم الصلاة والسّلام . قوله :(وزالت) أي حين جاءه البشير بقميص يوسف، كما أخبر الله تعالى بقوله : فَارْتَدَّ بَصِيرًا ) (1)
The ruling concerning sending messengers: Blind person has no basis, and Ya'qub had a cover and it was removed. As for forgetfulness (as-sahw): it is permissible in actions like the salutation from two rak'ahs, but not in statements. As for forgetting rulings (nasyan al-ahkam): it is not permissible for them before delivery, and it is permissible after delivery for its preservation, and because the messenger is required to preserve it to act by it and to deliver it. Forgetting the abrogated (al-mansukh) is permissible absolutely, before delivery and after. And know that what is permissible for them of human attributes that do not lead to deficiency in their high ranks is only according to their outward appearances; but their inward parts are filled with divine secrets, attached to love of the Creator of creation, so no distress, complaint, or sigh occurs from them; indeed, it increases them only in closeness and love. Indeed, this condition occurs in many of their nation, so how much more so for them, peace and blessings be upon them. His statement: 'and it was removed' means when the bearer of good news came with Yusuf's shirt, as Allah informed in His saying: 'So he turned back seeing' (12:96).
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage discusses the human attributes permissible for prophets and the rulings on forgetfulness. It begins by stating that 'blind person has no basis' (perhaps referring to a claim about a prophet being blind), and then mentions that Ya'qub (Jacob) experienced a veil that was removed. It then explains that forgetfulness (as-sahw) is allowed in actions (like the Prophet's salam from two rak'ats) but not in statements. Forgetting rulings is not allowed before delivering them, but after delivery it is permissible because the prophet is required to preserve the ruling for acting and delivering. Forgetting the abrogated is allowed absolutely. Then it clarifies that any human attributes that do not cause deficiency in their high ranks are only outward; inwardly, they are filled with divine secrets and love of Allah, so they do not feel distress. This state is found even among many of their followers, so it is even more so for the prophets. The marginal note explains that 'zālat' (was removed) refers to when the shirt of Yusuf was brought to Ya'qub, restoring his sight, referencing Quran 12:96.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any human imperfection in prophets, like forgetfulness or illness, implies a flaw in their spiritual rank.
Correction: The passage clarifies that such attributes are only outward and do not affect their inward perfection; they are free from distress and deficiency.

Checkpoint

B) They may not forget rulings at all.
C) They may forget rulings only after delivering them.

Key Takeaway
Forgetfulness in prophets is contextually permissible, and their human attributes only affect outward appearances, never their inner spiritual perfection.

Sending Messengers: Divine Favor or Obligation?
Refutes Mu'tazila and others on the necessity of sending messengers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why sending messengers is a divine favor and mercy, not an obligation upon Allah, and why the Mu'tazila's view based on rational obligation is incorrect.

Core Idea
Sending messengers is a gift from Allah, not a duty He owes.

This lesson examines the theological debate about whether Allah is obligated to send messengers. The author firmly states that sending messengers is a favor (tafaddul) and mercy, not a duty. He refutes the Mu'tazila who claim it is obligatory based on rational principles, as well as other sects who deny its necessity. The key point is Allah's absolute freedom as the 'free agent' (al-fā'il al-mukhtār).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to get the overall argument.
Notice the author's concise style and the embedded refutations.
2
Identify the main claim
Find the statement that sending messengers is tafaddul (favor) and rahma (mercy). Underline the phrase 'ليس بواجب عليه' (not obligatory upon Him).
3
Understand the Mu'tazila position
The Mu'tazila obligate sending messengers based on 'wujub al-salah' and 'al-aslah'. Recognize how the author counters this by invoking Allah's free agency.
This is a key difference between Ahl al-Sunna and Mu'tazila.
4
See the refutation of other sects
Note that the Sumaniyya and Barahima reject messengers as futile, and philosophers see them as natural. The author's statement refutes all of them.
The commentary clarifies that only Mu'tazila are sinners, while the others are disbelievers.
5
Reflect on divine free will
Consider why Allah's attribute as 'free agent' (fā'il mukhtār) excludes any obligation. Think about how this protects tawhid.
This connects to the broader Aqeedah of the Salaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إرسال الرّسل تفضّل ورحمة من الله. ولمَّا أوجبت المعتزلة إرسال الرُّسل بناءً على قاعدتهم، من وجوب الصَّلاح عليه تعالى، والأصلحُ في حقّ عبيده أن يُرسل إليهم الرُّسل لينبهوهم على ما يُنجيهم من المهالك وما يُوبقهم فيها، وأحاله السمنية والبراهمة نظراً إلى أنّه عبث ؛ لكون العقل كافياً عنه، أشار إلى الرّدّ عليهم بقوله : إرسالهم (تفضَّل وإحسان من الله تعالى، (ورحمة) منه (للعالمين) وليس بواجب عليه لما علمتَ أنَّه الفاعل المختار الذي لا حرج عليه ولا يُسأل عما يفعل ولا بمستحيل ؛ لأنّ العقل إذا خلا ونفسَه قد يغفل عن أكثر الأحوال المناسبة له في معاشه، فكيف بدقائق الشّرع والسَّمعيَّات التي لا تُتلقّى إلّا من الصَّادق . من (جل مولي) بضم الميم وكسر اللام؛ أي: معطي، (النعمة) التي أجلّها إرسال الرّسل إلينا فله الحمد على ذلك، وعلى كل حال. قوله : (نظراً إلى أنَّه عبث ... إلخ ) : أي : فهو بناء على أصلهم الفاسد من التحسين والتقبيح العقليين. قوله : (أشار للرَّدِّ عليهم) : أي : الفرق الثَّلاث، وكذا على الفلاسفة القائلين : إنَّ الرُّسل موجودون بالعلَّة والطبيعة، لكنَّ السُّمنية، والبراهمة، والفلاسفة كفَّار، والمعتزلة فساق . قوله: (فله الحمد على ذلك) : أي : على إرسال الرُّسل لنا ولم يدعنا كالبهائم هملاً .
Sending messengers is a favor and mercy from Allah. When the Mu'tazila obligated sending messengers based on their principle of the necessity of what is right for Him, and that the best for His servants is to send messengers to them to alert them of what saves them from destruction and what causes them to perish, and the Sumaniyya and Barahima rejected it, considering it futile because the intellect is sufficient for it, he indicated the refutation of them by his saying: Sending them (is a favor and beneficence from Allah, and mercy from Him (for the worlds) and it is not obligatory upon Him because you know that He is the free agent Who is not constrained and is not asked about what He does, nor is it impossible; because the intellect, when left to itself, may neglect most of the suitable circumstances for its livelihood, so how about the subtle matters of the law and scriptural things that are only received from the truthful. From (Jall Mawla), with damm on the meem and kasr on the lam: meaning the Giver, (the grace) whose greatest is sending messengers to us. So praise be to Him for that and for every state. His statement: 'considering it futile... etc.' means: it is based on their corrupt principle of rational tahsin and taqbiih. His statement: 'indicated the refutation of them' means: the three sects, and also the philosophers who say that messengers exist by cause and nature, but the Sumaniyya, Barahima, and philosophers are disbelievers, and the Mu'tazila are sinners. His statement: 'so praise be to Him for that' means: for sending messengers to us and not leaving us like cattle aimlessly.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage refutes those who deny or obligate the sending of messengers. It begins by stating that sending messengers is a favor (tafaddul) and mercy from Allah. It then presents the Mu'tazila position: they obligate it based on their principle that Allah must do what is right (al-salah) and that the best for His servants is to send messengers. The Sumaniyya and Barahima reject it, claiming it is futile since intellect is sufficient. The author responds by quoting: 'Sending them is a favor and beneficence from Allah, and mercy for the worlds, and it is not obligatory upon Him'. This is because Allah is the free agent, not constrained, and intellect alone is insufficient for subtle matters of revelation. The marginal notes explain that the Mu'tazila's view is based on their corrupt principle of rational tasheeh and taqbeeh. Another note clarifies that the refutation covers three sects (Mu'tazila, Sumaniyya, Barahima) and also the philosophers, stating that the Sumaniyya, Barahima, and philosophers are disbelievers, while Mu'tazila are sinners. The final note praises Allah for sending messengers and not leaving us aimless.

فاعل مختار
وجوب الصلاح
تحسين وتقبيح عقليان
سمنية
براهمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah is obligated to send messengers because it is the best (al-aslah) for His servants.
Correction: Allah is not obligated; sending messengers is a favor and mercy, not a duty, because He is the free agent who does as He wills.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is sending messengers not obligatory upon Allah?
A) Because messengers cannot bring benefit.
B) Because Allah is the free agent and cannot be compelled.
C) Because intellect alone suffices for all guidance.
D) Because the Mu'tazila proved it.

Key Takeaway
Sending messengers is a free gift of Allah's mercy, not a requirement imposed upon Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly see the sending of the Prophet ﷺ as a sheer mercy from Allah, or do you sometimes act as if Allah owed you guidance? What would change in your daily gratitude if you fully internalized that prophethood was a free gift you never deserved?
?

?
The passage ends with praise to Allah for not leaving us 'like cattle aimlessly.' In what areas of your life are you still wandering aimlessly, ignoring the guidance that the messengers brought? What is one step you can take today to submit more fully to that guidance?

Why Sending Prophets Is Not Obligatory on God
Refutation of the obligation of prophethood with sectarian classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why sending prophets is a favor and not an obligation on God, and you will be able to identify the sects that hold the opposing view along with their status.

Core Idea
Sending prophets is God's favor, not His obligation.

This passage tackles an important objection: if intellect is sufficient for guidance, then sending prophets would be futile. The commentator refutes this by showing that God is a free agent and that intellect alone cannot access all truths. He then categorizes the groups that wrongly assert that prophecy is obligatory, distinguishing between disbelievers and sinners.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice how the commentator sets up the objection and then refutes it.
2
Understand the main argument
Identify the key points: (1) The claim that sending prophets is futile, (2) The response that it is a favor, not an obligation, (3) The reasons: God is free agent and intellect may neglect details.
The intellect's limitation in Sharia matters is crucial.
3
Examine the sectarian classification
Note the three sects (Sumanities, Brahmins, Philosophers) who are disbelievers, and the Mu'tazilites who are sinners. Understand that the former reject revelation entirely, while the latter hold a wrong theological view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نظراً إلى أنّه عبث؛ لكون العقل كافياً عنه، أشار إلى الرّدّ عليهم بقوله: إرسالهم تفضَّل وإحسان من الله تعالى، ورحمة منه للعالمين، وليس بواجب عليه لما علمتَ أنَّه الفاعل المختار الذي لا حرج عليه ولا يُسأل عما يفعل ولا بمستحيل؛ لأنّ العقل إذا خلا ونفسَه قد يغفل عن أكثر الأحوال المناسبة له في معاشه، فكيف بدقائق الشّرع والسَّمعيَّات التي لا تُتلقّى إلّا من الصَّادق. جل مولي النعمة التي أجلّها إرسال الرّسل إلينا فله الحمد على ذلك وعلى كل حال. قوله: (نظراً إلى أنَّه عبث ... إلخ): أي: فهو بناء على أصلهم الفاسد من التحسين والتقبيح العقليين. قوله: (أشار للرَّدِّ عليهم): أي: الفرق الثَّلاث، وكذا على الفلاسفة القائلين: إنَّ الرُّسل موجودون بالعلَّة والطبيعة، لكنَّ السُّمنية، والبراهمة، والفلاسفة كفَّار، والمعتزلة فساق. قوله: (فله الحمد على ذلك): أي: على إرسال الرُّسل لنا ولم يدعنا كالبهائم هملاً.
Considering that it would be futile because the intellect is sufficient for it, he alluded to the refutation of them by his saying: 'Sending them is a favor and beneficence from Allah, and a mercy from Him to the worlds, and it is not obligatory upon Him because you have known that He is the free agent who is not constrained, nor is He asked about what He does, nor is it impossible; because the intellect, when left to itself, may neglect most of the suitable circumstances for it in its livelihood, so how about the intricacies of the Sharia and the transmitted matters which are only received from the truthful?' The Giver of the grace, the greatest of which is sending the messengers to us, so for Him is praise for that and for every situation. His saying: 'Considering that it would be futile... etc.': That is, it is based on their corrupt principle of rationalist (tahsin wa taqbiḥ 'aqli). His saying: 'He alluded to the refutation of them': That is, the three sects, and likewise against the philosophers who say that messengers exist by cause and nature, but the Sumenites, the Brahmins, and the philosophers are disbelievers, and the Mu'tazilites are sinners. His saying: 'So for Him is the praise for that': That is, for sending the messengers to us and not leaving us like cattle, neglected.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a commentary refuting the claim that sending prophets is obligatory upon God. The author first addresses the objection that if the intellect is sufficient, then sending prophets would be futile. He explains that this objection is based on the corrupt principle of rationalist (tahsin wa taqbiḥ 'aqli). The refutation is that sending prophets is a favor (tafaddul) and beneficence (ihsān) from God, not an obligation, because God is the free agent (al-fā'il al-mukhtār) who cannot be constrained. Moreover, the intellect alone may neglect many details needed in life, especially in matters of Sharia and transmitted knowledge (sam'iyyāt) which can only be received from truthful messengers. The author then identifies the groups that hold the opposing view: the three sects (al-firaq al-thalāth) — the Sumanites (al-Sumaniyya), the Brahmins (al-Barāhima), and the philosophers (al-Falāsifa) — are disbelievers (kuffār), while the Mu'tazilites are sinners (fussāq). Finally, he praises God for sending messengers and not leaving humanity neglected like cattle. The passage thus combines a theological proof with a sectarian classification.

Key Terms
تفضل (tafaddul)
إحسان (ihsān)
الفاعل المختار (al-fā'il al-mukhtār)
التحسين والتقبيح العقليين (al-taḥsīn wa al-taqbīḥ al-'aqliyyayn)
السمنية (al-Sumaniyya)
البراهمة (al-Barāhima)
الفلاسفة (al-Falāsifa)
المعتزلة (al-Mu'tazila)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God is obligated to send prophets for guidance, and that failing to do so would be unfair.
Correction: Sending prophets is not obligatory; it is a free act of grace (tafaddul) from God. God is the free agent and not subject to external obligations. The intellect is not fully sufficient; divine revelation is needed.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is sending prophets not obligatory upon God?
A) Because it would be futile if the intellect is sufficient.
B) Because God is the free agent who cannot be constrained or obligated.
C) Because the intellect is sufficient for all guidance.
D) Because the Mu'tazilites claim it is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Sending prophets is a free act of divine grace, not an obligation, and those who claim otherwise fall into error, with some becoming disbelievers and others sinners.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly feel sincere gratitude for the prophets sent to you, or do you take their guidance for granted? Imagine your life if Allah had left you 'like cattle, neglected' — what would that mean for your purpose and salvation? Commit today to reading the story of a prophet with fresh humility.
?
The passage warns that the intellect alone neglects many details of livelihood, let alone religious intricacies. In which practical area of your life are you trusting your own reasoning over prophetic guidance (e.g., business ethics, relationships)? Identify one specific decision this week where you will consciously seek prophetic wisdom first.
?
The commentator distinguishes between disbelievers and sinners based on their view of prophethood. Look at your own heart: do you subtly feel that God owes you guidance or salvation? Where does a sense of entitlement creep in? Repent from that and thank Allah that He sent messengers purely out of His favor.

Belief in the Prophets: Detailed and Summary
Obligation to believe in prophets and enumeration of 25 Quranic prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to believe in prophets, the distinction between detailed and summary belief, and the 25 prophets named in the Quran.

Core Idea
Believing in prophets means knowing the named ones and affirming the rest.

This passage establishes the central obligation of belief in the prophets sent by Allah. It distinguishes between two levels of belief: detailed belief in the prophets explicitly named in the Quran, and summary belief in all other prophets whose identities are not specified. The author also clarifies that 'detailed belief' does not require memorizing the list by heart, but rather affirming each prophet's prophethood when asked.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English translation. Notice that the passage begins by stating the obligation, then lists the 25 prophets, and ends with a clarification about detailed belief.
The list may be long, but it is important to recognize the names.
2
Identify the two types of belief
Look for the terms 'تفصيلاً' (in detail) and 'إجمالاً' (in summary). Understand that detailed belief applies to the named prophets, while summary belief applies to the rest.
Summary belief means affirming the existence of prophets not mentioned by name.
3
Understand the clarification on 'detailed'
Read the commentator's note about the meaning of 'تفصيلاً'. It does not require memorization; it means not denying any of them.
This addresses a common misunderstanding.
4
Reflect on the names
Count the listed prophets. There are 25. Think about why these particular prophets are emphasized.
These are the prophets explicitly mentioned in the Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثمّ يجب الإيمان بوجود الأنبياء عليهم الصَّلاة والسَّلام تفصيلاً فيما عُلِم منهم تفصيلاً، وهم المذكورون في القرآن؛ كمحمد عليه الصلاة والسلام وآدم ونوح وإدريس وهود وصالح واليسع وذي الكفل وإلياس ويونس - وهو ذو النون، أي: الحوت - وأيوب وإبراهيم وإسماعيل وإسحاق ويعقوب ويوسف ولوط و داود وسليمان وشعيب وموسى وهارون وزكريا ويحيى وعيسى، وإجمالاً فيما عُلم منهم إجمالاً.

وقد نظمهم العلامة العارف بالله السيد محمد الهاشمي في مفتاح الجنة» (ص ۲۳۸):
Then it is obligatory to believe in the existence of the prophets, peace be upon them, in detail regarding those known in detail, and they are those mentioned in the Qur'an: like Muhammad (peace be upon him), Adam, Noah, Idris, Hud, Salih, Al-Yasa', Dhul-Kifl, Ilyas, Yunus—and he is Dhul-Nun, i.e., the whale—Ayyub, Ibrahim, Isma'il, Ishaq, Ya'qub, Yusuf, Lut, Dawud, Sulayman, Shu'ayb, Musa, Harun, Zakariyya, Yahya, and 'Isa, and in summary regarding those known in summary. His statement: (in detail... etc.): The meaning is that if he were asked about any one of them, he would not deny that he is a prophet, even if he does not memorize their names by heart. And the scholar and mystic al-Sayyid Muhammad al-Hashimi has versified them in 'Miftah al-Jannah' (p. 238):
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage explains the obligation of belief in prophets. It states that one must believe in the existence of all prophets. For those prophets whose names and details are explicitly known from revelation (specifically the Qur'an), belief must be 'in detail' (tafsilan), meaning one must affirm each by name and not deny any of them. The passage then lists the twenty-five prophets mentioned in the Qur'an, starting with Muhammad and including Adam, Noah, Idris, Hud, Salih, Al-Yasa', Dhul-Kifl, Ilyas, Yunus, Ayyub, Ibrahim, Isma'il, Ishaq, Ya'qub, Yusuf, Lut, Dawud, Sulayman, Shu'ayb, Musa, Harun, Zakariyya, Yahya, and 'Isa. For prophets not mentioned in such detail (i.e., other prophets whose existence is known in general but not by name), one must believe 'in summary' (ijmalan), i.e., affirm that there were prophets sent by Allah without needing to know their names. The commentator then clarifies the meaning of 'detailed belief': it means that if asked about any of these named prophets, one would not deny his prophethood, even if one does not memorize the list by heart. Finally, he notes that the scholar al-Hashimi composed a poetic enumeration of these prophets in his work 'Miftah al-Jannah', though the full poem is not quoted here.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believing in detail requires memorizing the names of all the prophets by heart.
Correction: The commentator explains that detailed belief only requires not denying any of the named prophets when asked, even if one does not memorize their names.

Key Takeaway
Belief in prophets requires affirming the 25 named individuals in detail and all others in summary, without needing to memorize names.
