Belief in Prophets: Detailed and Summary Obligation
Al-Sawi states the obligation to believe in prophets, lists those in the Quran, and defines detailed belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two modes of belief in prophets: detailed for those named in the Quran and summary for those not named, and what 'detailed' belief entails.

Core Idea
Believe in all prophets, but you only need to know the names of those in the Quran.

Al-Sawi begins by stating the obligation to believe in all prophets. However, the mode of belief differs: for prophets mentioned in the Quran, belief must be specific; for others, it is general. This passage clarifies that 'detailed' belief does not require memorization but rather acknowledgment if asked.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on obligation
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the general command to believe in prophets, distinguishing between 'detailed' and 'summary'.
Notice the list of names is given as examples.
2
Understand 'detailed' belief
The commentary explains that 'detailed' means if asked about any of these prophets, you would not deny them, even if you don't memorize the list.
This is a practical definition, not a memorization test.
3
Apply the distinction
Consider why some prophets require detailed belief and others only summary. The Quran is the source of certainty for those named.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ثمّ) يجب الإيمان بوجود (الأنبياء) عليهم الصَّلاة والسَّلام تفصيلاً فيما عُلِم منهم تفصيلاً، وهم المذكورون في القرآن؛ كمحمد عليه الصلاة والسلام وآدم ونوح وإدريس وهود وصالح واليسع وذي الكفل وإلياس ويونس - وهو ذو النون، أي: الحوت - وأيوب وإبراهيم وإسماعيل وإسحاق ويعقوب ويوسف ولوط وداود وسليمان وشعيب وموسى وهارون وزكريا ويحيى وعيسى، وإجمالاً فيما عُلم منهم إجمالاً. قوله : (تفصيلاً . . . إلخ) : المراد أنه بحيث لو سئل عن واحد منهم لم ينكر كونه نبيّاً، وإن لم يحفظ أسماءهم عن ظهر قلب. والأولى ترك حصرهم في عدد معيّن لقوله تعالى: (مِنْهُم مَّن فَصَصْنَا عَلَيْكَ وَمِنْهُم مَّن لَّمْ نَقْصُصْ عَلَيْكَ )، ولا يؤمن في ذكر العدد أن يُدخَل فيهم من ليس منهم لجواز أن يذكر أكثر من الواقع، أو يُخرج منهم من هو منهم إن كان العدد أقل وما روي أنّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سُئِل عن عددهم فقال: «مئة ألف وأربعة وعشرون ألفاً»، وفي رواية: «مئتا ألف وأربعة وعشرون ألفاً»، فخبر آحاد لا يفيد القطع، ولا عبرة بالظَّنِّ في باب الاعتقادات. قوله : (لا يفيد القطع) : أي : والكلام في الاعتقاديَّات، وهي لا تكون إلا بالقطعي.
(Then) it is obligatory to believe in the existence of the prophets, peace be upon them, in detail regarding those known in detail—and they are those mentioned in the Quran, such as Muhammad, peace be upon him, and Adam, Noah, Idris, Hud, Salih, al-Yasa', Dhu al-Kifl, Ilyas, Yunus—who is Dhu al-Nun, i.e., the fish—and Ayyub, Ibrahim, Isma'il, Ishaq, Ya'qub, Yusuf, Lut, Dawud, Sulayman, Shu'ayb, Musa, Harun, Zakariyya, Yahya, and 'Isa; and in summary regarding those known in summary. He said: '(In detail ... etc.)': meaning that if he were asked about any one of them, he would not deny that he is a prophet, even if he does not know their names by heart. And it is better to leave restricting them to a specific number due to His statement: 'Among them are those We have narrated to you and among them are those We have not narrated to you.' And one is not safe from error when specifying a number—it is possible that one includes those not among them if the number given is greater than reality, or excludes those who are among them if the number is less. And what is narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, was asked about their number and he said: 'One hundred and twenty-four thousand' and in another narration: 'Two hundred and twenty-four thousand' is a solitary report (khabar ahad) that does not yield certainty, and conjecture has no weight in matters of belief. He said: '(Does not yield certainty)': i.e., and the discussion is about matters of belief, and they are only established by what is certain.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition on the obligation of belief in prophets. It begins by stating the general requirement: one must believe in all prophets, but the mode of belief differs based on what is known. For those prophets explicitly named in the Quran—the author lists twenty-five—belief must be specific and detailed. For other prophets not mentioned, belief is required in summary without knowing their names. The commentary clarifies that 'detailed' belief means that if asked about any of these named prophets, one would not deny his prophethood, even if one does not memorize the names. The passage then addresses the issue of the total number of prophets. Citing the Quranic verse 'Among them are those We have narrated to you and among them are those We have not narrated to you' (Surah Ghafir 78), the author argues that it is better not to fix a specific number because it invites error: one might include someone who is not a prophet or exclude an actual prophet. He then discusses the hadith reporting the number 124,000 or 224,000, noting that it is a solitary report (khabar ahad) which does not produce certainty. Since matters of belief require definitive knowledge, such a report cannot be the basis for a doctrinal article of faith. The final comment underscores that belief (i'tiqad) must be founded on certainty (qat'), not conjecture (zann).

Key Terms
الأنبياء
تفصيلاً
إجمالاً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That one must be able to list all prophets from memory to have correct belief.
Correction: The passage clarifies that detailed belief only requires not denying them, not memorization.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'detailed belief' in a prophet entail?
A) Reciting the prophet's name from memory
B) Not denying that the person is a prophet if asked
C) Knowing the prophet's entire biography
D) Accepting only prophets mentioned in the Quran

Key Takeaway
Belief in prophets is obligatory; for those named in the Quran, it must be detailed, but this only requires acknowledging their prophethood, not memorizing names.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite or hear the names of prophets you rarely think about—like Idris, Hud, or Salih—do you truly believe in them as messengers of Allah with the same conviction you have for Prophet Muhammad? If your belief is weaker, what concrete step can you take today to strengthen it?
?
The lesson says you don't need to memorize names, but you must never deny anyone's prophethood. Have you ever casually joked or spoken disrespectfully about any prophet, even one you know little about? Repent now and resolve to guard your tongue.
?
Belief in prophets is an obligatory pillar of your iman. Is your belief merely intellectual assent, or does it move your heart to love and obey them? Ask Allah to make your belief in all His prophets a living reality that changes how you live today.

The Number of Prophets: Why It Is Not Definitively Known
Al-Sawi argues against fixing the number of prophets and explains why the hadith on the number is not authoritative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why it is better not to specify the total number of prophets and why the hadith on the number is not a basis for belief.

Core Idea
The total number of prophets is unknown; speculation has no place in matters of faith.

Al-Sawi now addresses the issue of the total number of prophets. Citing a Quranic verse, he argues that it is safer not to fix a number, as it could lead to error. He then discusses the famous hadith reporting 124,000 prophets, but notes it is a solitary report that does not yield certainty, which is required for beliefs.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument against specifying a number
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the reasoning: the Quran says some prophets are not mentioned, so any fixed number might include non-prophets or exclude real ones.
2
Examine the hadith on the number
The passage mentions two versions of a hadith: 124,000 and 224,000. Note that these are 'khabar ahad' (solitary reports).
3
Understand why conjecture is invalid
The author asserts that in matters of belief, only certainty (qat') is acceptable. Since the hadith is not certain, it cannot be used to define a creedal point.
This is a key principle in kalam: belief must be based on definitive proof.

(Then) it is obligatory to believe in the existence of the prophets, peace be upon them, in detail regarding those known in detail—and they are those mentioned in the Quran, such as Muhammad, peace be upon him, and Adam, Noah, Idris, Hud, Salih, al-Yasa', Dhu al-Kifl, Ilyas, Yunus—who is Dhu al-Nun, i.e., the fish—and Ayyub, Ibrahim, Isma'il, Ishaq, Ya'qub, Yusuf, Lut, Dawud, Sulayman, Shu'ayb, Musa, Harun, Zakariyya, Yahya, and 'Isa; and in summary regarding those known in summary. He said: '(Does not yield certainty)': i.e., and the discussion is about matters of belief, and they are only established by what is certain.

Citing the Quranic verse 'Among them are those We have narrated to you and among them are those We have not narrated to you' (Surah Ghafir 78), the author argues that it is better not to fix a specific number because it invites error: one might include someone who is not a prophet or exclude an actual prophet. He then discusses the hadith reporting the number 124,000 or 224,000, noting that it is a solitary report (khabar ahad) which does not produce certainty. Since matters of belief require definitive knowledge, such a report cannot be the basis for a doctrinal article of faith. The final comment underscores that belief (i'tiqad) must be founded on certainty (qat'), not conjecture (zann).

Key Terms
خبر آحاد
قطعي
ظن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the hadith about 124,000 prophets is definitive and must be believed as a matter of faith.
Correction: The passage clarifies that it is a khabar ahad, which does not produce certainty, and thus cannot be a basis for belief.

Checkpoint
Why does the author consider it better not to specify the total number of prophets?
A) Because the Quran explicitly forbids counting them
B) Because the hadith on the number is a solitary report that does not yield certainty
C) Because no hadith exists on the number
D) Because prophets cannot be counted

Key Takeaway
The number of prophets is not definitively known; the hadith on the number is not certain, so it is better not to fix a number in matters of belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Have you ever repeated a religious fact simply because it was widely said, without checking its authenticity? How will you change your approach to ensure your beliefs are built on certainty, not conjecture?

Not Fixing the Number of Prophets
The author advises against fixing the number of prophets and explains the evidentiary basis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why it is preferable not to fix a specific number for the prophets and how the principle of certainty (qat‘) applies to matters of belief.

Core Idea
Matters of belief require certainty, and a hadith that is not certain cannot settle the number of prophets.

The author addresses a common question about the number of prophets. He advises against fixing a number, citing a Quranic verse and a rational argument. He also addresses a famous hadith, explaining its epistemological status and why it does not provide the certainty needed for creedal matters.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the English translation. Let the author's own words and flow come through before you interpret.
Notice the inclusion of a Quranic verse and a hadith.
2
Identify the two arguments against fixing a number
The author gives two main reasons: the Quranic verse (Ghafir 40:78) and the logical risk of error in any fixed number. Find both in the text.
The Quranic verse shows that some prophets are not mentioned, so any fixed number might be incomplete.
3
Understand the critique of the hadith
The author mentions the hadith about 124,000 or 224,000 prophets but notes it is khabar ahad, which yields only probability (zann). In matters of belief, only certainty (qat‘) is acceptable. Reflect on why this distinction matters.
This connects to the broader principle that creedal matters cannot be based on probabilistic reports.

Source Text

الإيمان بالأنبياء (1) والأولى ترك حصرهم في عدد معيّن لقوله تعالى: (مِنْهُم مَّن فَصَصْنَا عَلَيْكَ وَمِنْهُم مَّن لَّمْ نَقْصُصْ عَلَيْكَ ) (1)، ولا يؤمن في ذكر العدد أن يُدخَل فيهم من ليس منهم لجواز أن يذكر أكثر من الواقع، أو يُخرج منهم من هو منهم إن كان العدد أقل وما روي أنّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سُئِل عن عددهم فقال: «مئة ألف وأربعة وعشرون ألفاً»، وفي رواية: «مئتا ألف وأربعة وعشرون ألفاً (2)، فخبر آحاد لا يفيد القطع، ولا عبرة بالظَّنِّ في باب الاعتقادات . قوله : (لا يفيد القطع) : أي : والكلام في الاعتقاديَّات، وهي لا تكون إلا بالقطعي .
Faith in the prophets. It is preferable not to restrict them to a specific number, due to His saying the Exalted: 'Among them are those We have narrated to you, and among them are those We have not narrated to you.' And one is not safe in mentioning the number from including among them those who are not of them, because it is possible that he mentions more than the reality, or that he excludes from them those who are of them if the number is less. And what has been narrated that the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, was asked about their number and he said: 'One hundred and twenty-four thousand,' and in another narration: 'Two hundred and twenty-four thousand' is a khabar ahad (single-narrator report) that does not yield certainty, and there is no consideration of conjecture in the realm of beliefs. His saying: 'does not yield certainty' means: and the discussion is concerning matters of belief, and they are not established except by what is certain.

Commentary
This passage advises against fixing a specific number for the prophets. The author begins by stating the preferred position: it is better not to fix a number, citing the Quranic verse (Ghafir 40:78) where Allah says some prophets are mentioned and some are not. He then explains the risk: if one asserts a number, one might mistakenly include a non-prophet or exclude a true prophet, whether the number is too high or too low. He then addresses the hadith reporting 124,000 or 224,000 prophets, noting that this is a khabar ahad (a report transmitted through a single chain) which does not provide certainty (qat'). Since matters of belief require certainty, such reports are not authoritative. The appended gloss clarifies that in beliefs, only definitive proofs are acceptable, so conjecture (zann) has no place.

Correction: The hadith is khabar ahad and does not provide the certainty required for matters of belief. Therefore, it cannot be used to fix a number.

Muhammad's Supreme Rank and Refuting al-Zamakhshari
Affirms Muhammad's superiority and refutes Zamakhshari's argument from Surat al-Takwir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic consensus on Prophet Muhammad's superiority over all creation, including angels, and the refutation of al-Zamakhshari's counter-argument based on Quranic context.

Core Idea
Prophet Muhammad is superior to all creation by consensus; apparent praise of angels is contextual, not comparative.

This passage from al-Sawi's commentary addresses a critical issue: the rank of Prophet Muhammad relative to all creation. While consensus holds he is the best, al-Zamakhshari controversially argued for Jibril's superiority using Surat al-Takwir. The author explains the Quranic context and the rhetorical principle of 'matching speech to situation' to refute this claim, reaffirming Muhammad's unmatched status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core belief
Read the first part where the author states the obligation to believe Muhammad is the best of creation, noting the universal scope (jinn, humans, angels).
The phrase 'أفضل الخلق على الإطلاق' emphasizes absolute superiority.
2
Recognize the opposing view
Find the mention of al-Zamakhshari's claim that Jibril is superior, and his proof from Surat al-Takwir (verses describing Jibril as 'noble messenger' and 'trustworthy').
Notice the contrast: Jibril is praised, while Muhammad is only described as 'not mad' in the same surah.
3
Understand the refutation using balagha
The refutation states that the Quran is at the highest level of eloquence, which means matching speech to context. The disbelievers had insulted both the intermediary (Jibril) and the Prophet (accusing him of madness).
The context is key: the verses respond to specific accusations, not a general comparison.
4
See the contextual application
Allah praised Jibril to counter the claim that the Prophet learned from him, and exonerated the Prophet from madness because he was known as truthful and trustworthy. A verse confirms their recognition of him.
The passage cites 'أَمْ لَمْ يَعْرِفُوا رَسُولَهُمْ' to show the disbelievers knew the Prophet's character.
5
Conclude with the evidence
The passage ends by asserting that Muhammad's superiority is indicated by 'أساطير الأولين والآخرين'—the well-known stories of the first and last, i.e., abundant proofs.
This reinforces the consensus position against the isolated opinion of Zamakhshari.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان مراتب الخلق ويجب اعتقاد أنّ محمداً صلى الله عليه وسلم وعليهم أجمعين أفضلهم وأنّه آخرهم، ويليه في الفضل : الخصال قوله : ( أفضلهم أي الأنبياء، ومن باب أولى غيرهم فهو أفضل الخلق على الإطلاق جنّاً وإنساً وملكاً، دنيا وأخرى في جميع بإجماع المسلمين، ما عدا الزَّمخشري ؛ فإنَّه خرق الإجماع، وقال بتفضيل جبريل على محمد و مستدلاً بما في سورة التكوير من قوله تعالى: إِنَّهُ لَقَولُ رَسُولٍ كَرِيمٍ ... الآية (1) ، حيث وصف جبريل بأنه رسول كريم إلى قوله : (أمين (2) ، واقتصر في وصف محمد لله على قوله : (وَمَا صَاحِبُكُم بِمَجْنُونِ ) (3). فردَّ عليه : بأنَّ القرآن في أعلى طبقات البلاغة ؛ وهي مطابقة الكلام لمقتضى الحال ؛ فإنَّ كلام الكفَّار كان في الواسطة الذي كان يأخذ عنه النَّبيَّ ، حيث قالوا : إنَّما يعلمه بشر، وقالوا : إِنَّ به جِنَّة ؛ أي: أخذاً من الجنّ، فردَّ عليهم المولى بمدح الواسطة وبراءة المصطفى مما يقولون؛ فإنَّه كان معروفاً بينهم بالصَّادق الأمين قال تعالى: أَمْ لَمْ يَعْرِفُوا رَسُوهُمْ فَهُمْ لَهُ منكرون (4) ، وتفضيله دلّ عليه أساطير الأولين والآخرين.
Explanation of the ranks of creation. It is obligatory to believe that Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him and upon them all, is the best of them and that he is the last of them, and that next in virtue are the [excellent] traits. His saying: 'the best of them' meaning the prophets, and by even greater reason others, so he is the best of creation absolutely, jinn, humans, and angels, in this world and the next, in all [aspects], by consensus of the Muslims, except al-Zamakhshari; for he broke the consensus and said that Jibril is superior to Muhammad, arguing by what is in Surat al-Takwir from His saying: 'Indeed, it is the word of a noble messenger...' (1), where he described Jibril as a noble messenger up to His saying: 'trustworthy' (2), and he restricted in describing Muhammad peace be upon him to His saying: 'And your companion is not mad' (3). And it was refuted against him: that the Quran is in the highest levels of eloquence, which is the matching of speech to the requirement of the situation. Indeed, the speech of the disbelievers was concerning the intermediary from whom the Prophet used to take, when they said: 'Only a human teaches him,' and they said: 'He is possessed by jinn' meaning, receiving from the jinn. So the Lord refuted them by praising the intermediary and exonerating the Chosen One from what they said; for he was known among them as the truthful and trustworthy. He said Exalted: 'Or did they not recognize their Messenger, so they deny him?' (4). And his superiority is indicated by the legends of the first and the last.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage outlines the ranks of creation, focusing on the superior status of Prophet Muhammad. The author begins by stating the obligation to believe that Muhammad is the best of the prophets and the last of them, and that the next in virtue are 'al-khisal' (possibly a heading). In a gloss, he explains 'best of them' means of the prophets, and by even greater reason, of all others, so he is absolutely the best of all creation—jinn, humans, and angels—in this world and the next, by consensus of Muslims. He then notes that al-Zamakhshari broke this consensus by claiming that the angel Jibril is superior to Muhammad, basing his argument on a verse from Surah al-Takwir where Jibril is called a 'noble messenger' and 'trustworthy,' while in the same surah Muhammad is only described as 'not mad.' The refutation is given: the Quran's eloquence matches the context. The disbelievers were accusing the intermediary (Jibril) of teaching Muhammad and claiming the Prophet was possessed by jinn. Thus Allah praised the intermediary (Jibril) to counter their slur about him, and exonerated the Prophet from the charge of madness. The Prophet was known among them as truthful and trustworthy, as indicated in another verse. Therefore, the apparent praise of Jibril is not a comparison but a contextual response. The superiority of Muhammad is established by abundant proofs, described as 'the legends of the first and the last' (well-known stories).

Key Terms
أفضل الخلق
إجماع
البلاغة
مقتضى الحال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verses in Surat al-Takwir show that Jibril is superior to Prophet Muhammad.
Correction: The verses are a contextual response to disbelievers who insulted both Jibril and Muhammad; Jibril is praised in that context, not compared. The overall consensus and abundant proofs establish Muhammad's superiority.

Checkpoint
What argument did al-Zamakhshari use to claim that Jibril is superior to Muhammad, and how is it refuted?
A) He cited a verse praising Jibril as a noble messenger, but the refutation shows the verse is a contextual response to disbelievers' insults.
B) He argued that angels are inherently superior, but the refutation says Muhammad's prophethood outweighs angelic status.
C) He claimed Jibril is the best of all creation because he was sent to the Prophet, but the refutation says Muhammad is superior by consensus.
D) He said the Quran calls Jibril 'trustworthy,' but Muhammad is not called that, but the refutation says Muhammad is called trustworthy elsewhere.

Key Takeaway
Prophet Muhammad is the best of all creation by consensus, and the apparent praise of angels in the Quran is context-specific, not a basis for comparison.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been falsely accused, and felt the urge to defend yourself angrily? The Prophet was called a madman and taught by others, yet Allah defended him by praising the intermediary and exonerating him with calm wisdom. When you face slander, can you respond by highlighting the truth about others involved rather than lashing out? This week, before reacting to any false accusation, pause and ask: 'What would be the eloquent response that matches the situation?'
?
Al-Zamakhshari broke the consensus of Muslims on Muhammad's superiority based on a superficial reading of one verse. Are there any beliefs you hold that go against the mainstream understanding of the Quran and Sunnah? Are you willing to subject your views to the principle of context and the consensus of scholars? Commit to seeking the tafsir of any verse you might be misinterpreting due to lack of context.
?
This lesson teaches that the Quran's eloquence means every word is perfectly placed. When you recite verses about the prophets, do you reflect on why Allah chose those specific words and the situation they address? The Ruling on Denying the Mi'raj and Isra
Author lists obligatory beliefs and explains the ruling on denying the Mi'raj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the Isra and Mi'raj and the corresponding rulings for those who deny them.

Core Idea
Denying the Isra is disbelief, but denying only the Mi'raj is a major sin.

The author first provides examples of obligatory beliefs conveyed by the Prophet, then focuses on the events of the Isra and Mi'raj. He clarifies a common confusion: the term 'Mi'raj' sometimes includes the Isra, but they are distinct. This distinction is crucial for correctly judging those who reject these events.

Guided Path
1
Identify the list of obligatory beliefs
Read the opening part of the passage where the author enumerates examples of obligations, prohibitions, and permissibility brought by the Prophet. Note that these are all from the 'samiyyat' (revealed matters).
These examples set the context for the discussion of the Mi'raj.
2
Understand the description of the Mi'raj
Focus on the details: the Mi'raj was with the body while awake, after the Isra, with Jibril but without Buraq (according to the relied-upon view). The Isra involved riding Buraq from Mecca to Jerusalem.
The author emphasizes that the Mi'raj and Isra are distinct events.
3
Analyze the objection and answer
Note the objection: why call the denier of the Mi'raj a kafir? The author responds that when he says 'denier of the Mi'raj', he means denier of the Isra, which is kufr. Denying only the Mi'raj (without Isra) makes one a fasiq.
This shows the importance of precise terminology in issuing rulings.
4
Reflect on the nuance
Consider how this lesson guards against blanket judgments. Not every detail of the Mi'raj is a matter of faith to the same degree. Only the Isra (the night journey) is considered necessary to believe.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كوجوب شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله وأن محمداً رسول الله، وإقام الصلاة، وإيتاء الزكاة وصوم رمضان، وحج بيت الله الحرام، وحرمة الزِّنا والخمر والرِّبا ، وحِلَّ النكاح والبيع، ونحو ذلك . - وكالمعراج بجسده الشريف ، يقظة، وهو العروج إلى السماء مع جبريل بلا براق بعد الإسراء، ليلاً من المسجد الحرام إلى المسجد الأقصى راكباً للبراق، وهو دابَّة أبيض طويل، فوق الحمار، ودون البغل، يضع حافره عند منتهى طرفه، والمراد بالمعراج ما يعم الإسراء، وقصته مشهورة. - وكسؤال المَلَكَين

Such as the obligation of the testimony that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, establishing prayer, giving zakat, fasting Ramadan, pilgrimage to the Sacred House of Allah, the prohibition of adultery, wine, and usury, the permissibility of marriage and trade, and similar matters. Commentary
This passage begins with a list of obligatory beliefs that come from the Prophet (al-bashir), including the shahada, pillars of Islam, prohibitions, and permissibilities. It then focuses on the event of the Mi'raj, describing its details: it was with the body while awake, after the Isra (night journey) to Jerusalem, ascending to heaven with Jibril without Buraq according to the relied-upon view. An objection is raised: why judge the denier of Mi'raj as a kafir? The answer is that the Mi'raj in context includes the Isra, so only denying the Isra incurs kufr. This nuance is important for correct judgment.

Correction: Only denial of the Isra (night journey from Mecca to Jerusalem) is disbelief; denial of the Mi'raj itself (the ascension) is a major sin but not kufr.

Dhul-Qarnayn's Dam: Human Effort Under Divine Decree
Describes how Dhul-Qarnayn built a dam with iron and copper to restrain Gog and Magog.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the story of Dhul-Qarnayn's dam and its lesson that all human effort succeeds only with Allah's permission and according to His timing.

Core Idea
Dhul-Qarnayn's dam shows that human effort succeeds only with Allah's permission.

This passage recounts the construction of a mighty barrier by the righteous king Dhul-Qarnayn to contain Gog and Magog. The story illustrates how human actions are intertwined with divine decree, emphasizing that no matter how strong a barrier, it cannot hold back what Allah has ordained. As you read, notice the sequence of building and the miraculous restoration each night.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the narrative flow without over-analyzing.
2
Analyze the construction method
Identify the materials Dhul-Qarnayn used (rock, iron, molten copper) and the two-phase building process: first over water, then above ground with iron and copper.
This shows his resourcefulness and determination.
3
Examine the digging cycles
Notice the pattern: Gog and Magog dig each day nearly succeeding, but then their leader says 'go back, you will dig tomorrow' – and Allah restores the dam stronger. What does this teach about human power versus divine power?
The addition of 'if Allah wills' at the end is crucial.
4
Reflect on divine timing
The passage ends when Allah decides to release them. How does this story reinforce the belief that events only happen by Allah's decree and at His appointed time?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلما رأى ذلك ذو القرنين؛ شرع في بناء السد واهتم به، فبنى الجدار على الماء بالصَّخر والحديد والنُّحاس المذاب، فلما وصل إلى ظاهر الأرض ؛ بنى بقطع الحديد وأفرغ عليه النحاس المذاب. روي أنَّهم يحفرونه كلَّ يوم حتّى إذا كادوا يخرقونه، قال الذي عليهم: ارجعوا فستحفرونه غداً، فيعيده الله كأشدَّ ممَّا كان، حتَّى إذا بلغ مدتهم وأراد الله أن يبعثهم إلى النَّاس ؛ قال الذي عليهم : ارجعوا فستحفرونه غداً إن شاء الله فيرجعون فيجدونه على هيئته حين تركوه فيخرجون منه إلى النَّاس فيستسقون المياه وتنفر النَّاس منهم
When Dhul-Qarnayn saw that, he began building the dam and took care of it. He built the wall over water with rock, iron, and molten copper. When he reached the surface of the earth, he built with pieces of iron and poured molten copper over it. It is narrated that they dig it every day until they almost break through; then the one in charge says: go back, you will dig it tomorrow. So Allah returns it stronger than it was. Until when their time comes and Allah wants to send them to the people, the one in charge says: go back, you will dig it tomorrow if Allah wills. So they return and find it as they left it, then they come out to the people and they seek water from them and the people flee from them.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage narrates the story of Dhul-Qarnayn's dam, built to confine Gog and Magog. Using rock, iron, and molten copper, he constructed an impenetrable barrier over water. The narration describes how Gog and Magog attempt to dig through daily but are thwarted: each day they dig until almost breaking through, then their leader says 'tomorrow we will dig', but Allah restores the dam stronger than before. This continues until God's appointed time. When their release is decreed, the leader adds 'if Allah wills', and the dam remains as they left it, allowing them to emerge. Once out, they will cause chaos, demanding water and terrifying people. This story shows both human effort under divine guidance and the absolute control of Allah over such events.

Key Terms
ذو القرنين
سد
نحاس
حديد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the dam was built by Alexander the Great.
Correction: The text identifies the builder as Dhul-Qarnayn, who is a figure in the Quran, distinct from Alexander. The story is from Islamic tradition.

Checkpoint
What materials did Dhul-Qarnayn use to build the dam?
A) Wood and clay
B) Rock, iron, and copper
C) Bricks and mortar
D) Straw and mud

Key Takeaway
The story emphasizes that no matter how strong a barrier, it cannot hold back what Allah has decreed, and that divine timing alone determines events.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you plan something important, do you genuinely attach your will to Allah's decree by saying 'In sha Allah' with your heart, or is it just a habit? How would your actions change if you truly believed that no barrier can hold back what Allah has decreed? Ask yourself now: In what area of your life have you been relying on your own strength instead of acknowledging Allah's ultimate control? Commit to one specific change this week that reflects reliance on Allah's timing and power.
?
The leader's omission of 'in sha Allah' caused the dam to be restored; its inclusion allowed the release. Think of a recent situation where you either said or did not say 'if Allah wills' about a future event. Did that reflect your actual reliance on Allah? What would it look like to live every moment with the consciousness that your efforts are nothing without His permission? Resolve to start today by saying 'in sha Allah' meaningfully before every plan.
?
Gog and Magog almost break through every day, but Allah restores the dam stronger each time—until the appointed time. What 'almost' moments have you faced where Allah intervened? Are you trusting that His restoration is always better, even if you don't see it immediately? This week, whenever you face a setback, pause and say: 'Allah will restore it stronger than before.' How would that change your reaction?

Prophethood
intermediate

Prophetic Attributes from the Second Shahada
Enumerates prophetic attributes entailed by the second shahada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the declaration of Muhammad's messengership logically entails a set of essential prophetic attributes, including truthfulness, trustworthiness, and infallibility.

Core Idea
The second part of the Shahada logically demands belief in prophetic infallibility and essential human traits.

In this lesson, we explore the doctrinal implications of the second half of the Shahada, "Muhammad is the Messenger of God." The source passage from a classical Aqeedah text unpacks how this simple statement necessitates a series of prophetic attributes that shape Sunni theology regarding prophethood. By understanding these entailments, we grasp why the Prophet must be truthful, trustworthy, intelligent, and protected from sin and error.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation. Notice the author's systematic listing of attributes.
The passage is dense and logically structured.
2
Identify each prophetic attribute
Find and note each attribute that the passage states is necessarily entailed by messengerhood: truthfulness, trustworthiness, conveying rulings, intelligence, infallibility, and the impossibility of their opposites.
Also note the permissibility of certain human attributes.
3
Understand the logical connections
Reflect on why each attribute is logically necessary. For example, a messenger must be truthful, otherwise the message is unreliable.
This is a central theme in kalam.
4
Apply the lesson to belief in all he brought
The passage concludes that his truthfulness necessitates belief in everything he brought. Consider how this ties the attributes to the broader creed.
This includes belief in all prophets and messages.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجملة الثانية وهي قولنا : محمد رسول الله : فقد دلّت على ثبوت الرِّسالة له ، وذلك يستلزم صدقه في كلّ ما أخبر به، وأمانته، وتبليغه للعباد كلَّ ما أُمِر بتبليغه من الأحكام، وفطانته، إذ الرَّسول لا يكون إلا معصوماً، واستحالة أضدادها عليه ، وجواز كل ما لا يؤدّي إلى نقص في علو مرتبته من الأعراض البشرية . ووجوب صدقه يستلزم الإيمان بكلِّ ما جاء به، ومن ذلك إرسال
And as for the second sentence, which is our statement: Muhammad is the Messenger of God, it has indicated the establishment of messengerhood for him, and that necessitates his truthfulness in everything he informed of, his trustworthiness, his conveying to the servants everything he was commanded to convey of the rulings, his intelligence, for the messenger is not except infallible, and the impossibility of their opposites for him, and the permissibility of everything that does not lead to a deficiency in the loftiness of his rank from human attributes. And the necessity of his truthfulness necessitates belief in everything he brought, and from that is the sending [of messengers?]
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage discusses the second part of the Shahada, 'Muhammad Rasul Allah'. The author says that this sentence establishes the messengerhood of the Prophet, and that messengerhood necessarily entails a set of prophetic attributes: truthfulness in all his reports, trustworthiness (amanah), full delivery of the revealed rulings, intelligence (fatanah), and infallibility ('ismah) – since a messenger must be protected from sin and error. Consequently, the opposites of these attributes are impossible for him. Additionally, it permits for the prophet all human traits that do not detract from his high rank. Finally, the necessity of his truthfulness logically requires believers to accept and believe in everything he brought from God, including the sending of messengers (or other doctrines).

Key Terms
الرسالة
الصدق
الأمانة
التبليغ
الفطانة
العصمة
الأعراض البشرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets are infallible only in conveying revelation but can err in other matters.
Correction: The passage states that a messenger is 'not except infallible' (لا يكون إلا معصوماً), indicating that infallibility is a general attribute of the messenger as such, covering all aspects of his mission.

Checkpoint
What does the second part of the Shahada necessitate regarding the Prophet's reports?
A) He may sometimes be mistaken.
B) He must be truthful in everything he informs of.
C) He is only truthful in religious matters.
D) He does not need to convey all rulings.

Key Takeaway
The second shahada logically requires us to affirm that the Prophet is truthful, trustworthy, intelligent, and infallible, and to believe in everything he brought from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah', do you truly accept that he is completely truthful in everything he said? Is there any teaching of the Prophet that you find hard to embrace? What does that resistance reveal about your trust in his messengerhood?
?
The Prophet is described as trustworthy in conveying every ruling. Do you treat the rulings of Islam as a complete package, or do you selectively follow what suits you? Which command do you most struggle to implement, and what concrete step can you take this week to align with his perfect conveyance?
?
If the messenger is infallible, his example is flawless. Which of his sunnah do you find most difficult to follow? How can you increase your consistency in that area starting today, knowing that he is the perfect role model?

Prophethood
intermediate
5 min
What the Second Shahada Implies
Al-Sawi explains the implications of the second shahada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the second shahada logically necessitates prophethood's essential attributes and requires belief in all revealed matters (sam'iyyat).

Core Idea
The second shahada is a comprehensive affirmation that entails prophethood and all revelation.

This passage unpacks what it truly means to declare that Muhammad is the Messenger of God. It shows that this declaration is not just a statement but a logical foundation for prophethood's attributes and for accepting everything he brought, including the unseen matters of faith. Al-Sawi demonstrates how each implication follows necessarily from the simple affirmation of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Al-Sawi uses a logical chain beginning with the second shahada.
2
Identify the attributes that prophethood necessitates
The passage lists several attributes that necessarily accompany prophethood: truthfulness, trustworthiness, conveyance of commands, intelligence, and infallibility. It also states the impossibility of their opposites and the permissibility of human accidents that do not lower his rank. Make a mental note of each attribute.
These attributes are necessary, not optional.
3
Trace the chain from truthfulness to faith
The necessity of the Prophet's truthfulness then compels belief in everything he brought. This includes belief in earlier messengers (and their necessary, impossible, and permissible attributes), scriptures, the Last Day, and all other matters known through revelation (sam'iyyat).
This shows the comprehensive nature of faith rooted in the shahada.
4
Reflect on the structure of the argument
Notice that Al-Sawi uses a logical deduction: if X (prophethood) then Y (truthfulness, etc.), and if Y then Z (faith in all that he brought). This is a classic kalam reasoning method.
Consider how this argument grounds the entire Islamic creed in a single statement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجملة الثانية وهي قولنا : محمد رسول الله : فقد دلت [؟] على ثبوت الرسالة له ، وذلك يستلزم صدقه في كل ما أخبر به، وأمانته، وتبليغه للعباد كل ما أمر بتبليغه من الأحكام، وفطانته، إذ الرسول لا يكون إلا معصوماً، واستحالة أضدادها عليه ، وجواز [؟] كل ما لا يؤدي إلى نقص في علو مرتبته من الأعراض البشرية . ووجوب صدقه يستلزم الإيمان بكل ما جاء به، ومن ذلك إرسال الرسل، وهو يستلزم ما يجب في حقهم، وما يستحيل وما يجوز، والإيمان بسائر الكتب السماوية، واليوم الآخر، والحساب، وما عطف عليه مما مر من جميع السمعيات .
As for the second sentence, which is our saying: 'Muḥammad is the Messenger of God,' it has indicated [؟] the establishment of message (risāla) for him, and that necessitates his truthfulness in everything he informed of, his trustworthiness, his conveying to the servants everything he was commanded to convey of rulings, his intelligence, since the messenger is only infallible, and the impossibility of their opposites for him, and the permissibility of [؟] everything that does not lead to a deficiency in the elevation of his rank from human accidents. And the necessity of his truthfulness necessitates faith in everything he brought, and from that is the sending of messengers, and it necessitates what is obligatory in their regard, what is impossible and what is permissible, and faith in the rest of the heavenly books, the Last Day, the Reckoning, and what is appended to it from what has passed of all the samʿiyyāt (matters known through revelation).
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage explains the implications of the second shahada, 'Muhammad is the Messenger of God'. The author states that this establishes his prophethood, which necessitates truthfulness, trustworthiness, conveyance of all commands, intelligence, and infallibility, and the impossibility of their opposites. It also permits human accidents that do not detract from his rank. The necessity of his truthfulness then requires faith in everything he brought, including the sending of messengers, which in turn entails what is obligatory, impossible, and permissible regarding them, and belief in all revealed matters (sam'iyyat) like scriptures, the Last Day, etc.

Key Terms
رسالة
صدق
عصمة
سمعيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think prophethood does not entail infallibility; here it asserts it is necessary.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that the messenger is only infallible (ma'sūm), meaning protection from sin and error is a necessary attribute of prophethood.

Checkpoint
What does the establishment of prophethood (risāla) for Muhammad necessarily entail regarding his character?
A) Truthfulness, trustworthiness, intelligence, and infallibility
B) Only truthfulness
C) Only infallibility
D) Only trustworthiness

Key Takeaway
The second shahada logically entails prophethood's necessary attributes and compels belief in all revealed doctrines, making it the cornerstone of Islamic faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that the Prophet (s) is truthful in everything he reported, what is one command from his sunnah that you have been neglecting? Why do you still ignore it?
?
The shahada you recite daily entails belief in all prophets before him. Do you truly honour and respect them all, or do you harbour any disrespect in your heart? What will you do to correct that?
?
This passage shows that believing in Muhammad (s) necessitates accepting all the unseen worlds. Does your heart truly settle on the reality of the Last Day, or do you live as if it is distant? What change must you make today to live with that certainty?
